================================================================================
  Annotated commit history -- Tilck
================================================================================

This file walks Tilck's first-parent master history in chronological order
(oldest first). Each commit has:

  - its verbatim git log header (hash, author, date, subject, body),
  - the body (when present) as a plain paragraph, and
  - an "AI notes" section summarizing what changed (mechanical, read
    directly off the diff) and, when non-obvious, a context line that
    guesses intent. Every guess is explicitly flagged as such.

Purpose: a pre-processed skim layer over `git log` so that an AI assistant
(or a human) can orient quickly without re-reading every diff. The source
of truth is always `git show <sha>`.

Commit-subject prefix convention: Tilck uses bracketed subsystem prefixes
in subjects -- [boot], [kernel], [mm], [sched], [fs], [vfs], [kb], [tty],
[pci], [acpi], [kmalloc], [signal], [term], [selftest], [gtests],
[toolchain], [build], [ci], [docs], [configurator], [pkgmgr], etc.
Multi-area commits use multiple brackets: [kernel][fs]. When a note says
"touches X subsystem" it is echoing that prefix plus the diff's file
layout.

================================================================================
  ERA 1 -- Cygwin / Bochs on Windows  (Mar 2016 - Aug 2016)
================================================================================

  Early exOS. Development happens on Windows 7/10 under Cygwin, debugged
  in Bochs. The bootloader is hand-written NASM; the kernel is a single
  C file compiled with Cygwin-gcc and linked with the pei-i386 default
  linker script (so symbols carry the underscore prefix). Much of the
  early interrupt / IDT / IRQ scaffolding is adapted from Bran's
  Kernel Development Tutorial, a common starting point for osdev
  hobbyists of the era. By the end of this era Tilck has: a 2-stage
  bootloader, a 32-bit higher-half kernel at 0xC0100000, basic paging
  with map_page / unmap_page / pdir_clone, a physical page bitmap, a
  VGA text-mode console with scrollback, a keyboard driver with
  E0-extended scancodes, and a first ring-3 transition via a synthetic
  iret frame. Everything still lives in per-directory hand-written
  Makefiles; no unit tests, no CI, no .gitignore.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## dc675409 -- saving the first code with protected mode barely OK

Commit: dc675409db7f1d2d4d3747ae7e525332d17f301b
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 5 19:05:45 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  initial snapshot. Five new files, 692 lines:

  - myboot.asm (138 l.) -- 512-byte first-stage MBR bootloader: sets up a 4K
    stack, calls BIOS int 13h to load one group of 18 sectors from the floppy at
    ES:BX = 0x2000:0, then jumps there.

  - kernelBase.asm (343 l.) -- second-stage loaded at 0x20000: defines a 3-entry
    GDT (null/code/data) plus a 2048-byte IDT area, includes
    realModeStrings.asm, enables the A20 line, sets CR0.PE, and (attempts to)
    jump into 32-bit code.

  - realModeStrings.asm (152 l.) -- real-mode BIOS print/number helpers shared
    by the two .asm files.

  - make_iso.sh (10 l.) -- nasm-compiles both .asm files and dds them into
    os2.img (MBR + stage2 at offset 512 x 1).

  - bochsrc.bxrc (49 l.) -- Bochs 2.6.8 configuration targeting os2.img as
    floppy A, Win32 host, magic_break enabled. The config references Windows
    paths (C:\Program Files (x86)\Bochs-2.6.8,
    C:\Users\Vladislav\Desktop\os_dev\ex2) -- this is the Windows/Cygwin era
    described in docs/ancient_commits.md.

Context (guess -- no body):

  the starting point of what would become Tilck (initially "exOS"). The
  subject's "barely OK" reflects that the protected-mode switch works well
  enough to run *something*, but the scaffolding is still shaky -- follow-up
  commits fix the far-jump, A20 timing, etc.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## a3f901b5 -- reading more data from floppy, seems to work

Commit: a3f901b52dc6cc0af3ddef3bb115737b232bd49c
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 5 19:39:42 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  myboot.asm gains a load loop. Previous code did a single int 13h read of 18
  sectors; now it starts at sector 1, advances a [counter] by 18 each iteration
  up to 108 total sectors (~=54 KB), and computes the destination offset as
  counter*512 - 512 in BX so successive chunks are stored contiguously at ES:BX.
  Exit condition cmp ax, 108 ; jge ok.

Context (guess -- no body):

  the kernel image grew beyond what one BIOS floppy read could load, so the
  bootloader had to be taught to loop. 108 sectors is hardcoded.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## f999ea88 -- linking the C kernel. Still not working the JMP to it

Commit: f999ea88229fe6b0a8d2d9da219758c1adaa1e2e
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 5 20:54:29 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernelBase.asm -> renamed to boot_stage2.asm (similarity 96%); adds [ORG
    0x20000] at the top; stage2 is now padded to 8 KB (times 8192-($-$$) db 0)
    instead of 4 KB; the final asmMain now ends in jmp 0x22000 targeting the new
    C kernel.

  - New kernel32.c (13 l.) -- a placeholder _start() doing a = 0xAABBCCDD; b =
    0x00000011; c = a; c += b; (no side effects; intentional stub to verify
    linking).

  - make_iso.sh -- compiles kernel32.c with gcc -m32 -c -ffreestanding -nostdinc
    -fno-builtin, links with ld -r -Ttext 0x0 -s, extracts .text via objcopy -O
    binary, and dds the result to sector 17 of os2.img (i.e. right after the 8
    KB stage2).

Context (guess -- subject):

  first attempt to bring in C code. The near-jmp 0x22000 fails because the code
  segment selector hasn't been reloaded after the GDT -- that's what the next
  commit fixes.

## d9d2843d -- fixing jmp

Commit: d9d2843dc5839085a66e3faf26a9fc50aafca496
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 5 23:54:44 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  boot_stage2.asm replaces the near jmp 0x22000 with a far jmp dword
  0x08:0x00022000. 0x08 is the code selector from the new GDT, so this reload
  makes the jump actually enter 32-bit protected mode at the C kernel address.

Context (guess -- no body):

  follow-up to the previous commit's "Still not working the JMP to it". Standard
  bootloader foot-gun: you need a far jump after enabling PE to flush the
  pipeline with the right CS.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 342b9ff8 -- finally FULL 32 bit mode works.

Commit: 342b9ff8ccde4dd7107f0af8c345e6e08d2ac651
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 6 12:25:36 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  boot_stage2.asm reshuffles the protected-mode transition. The old flow (set PE
  -> data-segment reload at complete_flush -> call smart_enable_A20 -> far-jump
  to C) is reordered to: enable A20 while still in real mode, zero the IDTR (no
  IDT yet), set CR0.PE, far-jump 0x08:0x1000 into 32-bit complete_flush, reload
  DS/ES/FS/GS/SS = 0x10, then far-jump 0x08:0x00022000 to the C kernel. Dead
  8-nop delay removed; the speculative [0xb8000] character write is kept as a
  visual heartbeat.

Context (subject says it):

  celebration commit -- the first time 32-bit mode is entered cleanly
  end-to-end.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 41cca079 -- fixing .rdata: now we have a hello world in C

Commit: 41cca0794c19b961a7c89fbfc7522b235bbd4025
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 6 14:46:08 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel32.c grows from the 13-line placeholder to a minimal VGA text-mode
    driver: enum vga_color, make_color(), make_vgaentry(), term_init() fills the
    80x25 framebuffer at 0xB8000 with '*', and write_string() walks a C string
    with wrap-on-80.

  - kernelMain() now prints "hello from my kernel!   " and hangs in while(1).

  - boot_stage2.asm: reorders comments/debug xchg to make clearer that PE is set
    *before* the far jump (no behavioural change).

  - make_iso.sh: builds with -fno-asynchronous-unwind-tables, links via -T
    link.ld -Ttext 0x22000, objcopy now includes .rdata too.

Context (subject says it):

  .rdata inclusion was required so the string literal "hello from my kernel!"
  would make it into the final binary -- previously only .text was extracted.

## fda6e39f -- the .data section works as well

Commit: fda6e39f689158c5334a6d8c31f1fef4676168fc
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 6 20:19:52 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel32.c gains a statically initialized uint8_t mybuffer[16] with bytes
    0x11..0xFF; kernelMain() decrements each entry -- a write-then-read proof
    that .data is both loaded and writable.

  - make_iso.sh extracts a CFLAGS variable, adds -std=c99 -mno-red-zone, and
    includes .data in the objcopy section list.

## be903264 -- making the 2nd stage of bootloader just 4 KB

Commit: be903264c7378db21dab408e3c9063809f05d075
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 6 20:28:21 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - boot_stage2.asm: drops the unused idt times 2048 db 0 reservation, trims the
    complete_flush payload-copy loop from 4 KB to 1 KB, and changes the final
    far-jump destination from 0x00022000 to 0x00021000. Total stage2 padding
    drops from 8 KB to 4 KB.

  - make_iso.sh: kernel now linked at 0x21000 and written to sector 9 of the
    floppy (was sector 17).

Context (subject):

  shrinking the bootloader footprint by ~4 KB to give the kernel more room /
  reduce boot-time reads.

## 72d01ae6 -- copying about 512 from floppy for the kernel

Commit: 72d01ae6006de610f487a32eb00ade10cd2c0360
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 6 21:31:14 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - myboot.asm rewritten with [ORG 0x0000] and named macros (BASE_LOAD_ADDR =
    0x07C0, SECTORS_TO_READ_AT_TIME = 8, DEST_SEGMENT_KERNEL = 0x2000). Adds an
    outer big_load_loop that advances currSegmentKernel in steps of 0x1000 (i.e.
    64 KB segments), covering 0x20000..0xAFFFF -- ~512 KB of kernel space. Inner
    loop reads 8 sectors per int 13h call up to sector 128 per segment.

  - boot_stage2.asm: removes a stray [ORG 0x20000] (now relying on addressing
    done in stage1).

  - realModeStrings.asm: trivial comment reshuffle only.

Context (guess -- no body):

  the kernel was outgrowing the single-segment 64 KB limit; bootloader now loads
  up to ~512 KB across multiple segments.

## e79f363a -- adding several stuff to the kernel

Commit: e79f363a2005a243d62544c6f8e567dc67184762
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 7 01:32:24 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel32.c: significant expansion.

  - outb() / inb() inline wrappers (first port I/O helpers).

  - update_cursor(row, col) writing VGA CRTC index/data ports 0x3D4/0x3D5.

  - terminal_row/column/color promoted to volatile globals.

  - term_init() now clears with spaces (not '*') and resets cursor.

  - New term_write_char(c) handling '\n' and '\r'; write_string() rewritten on
    top of it.

  - New term_move_ch(row, col) for cursor positioning.

  - New itoa(value, str, base) -- the "zyxwvutsrqponmlkjihgfedcba..." index
    trick.

  - New show_hello_message() writing corners with * and two lines of text;
    kernelMain renamed to kmain().

  - New kernelAsm.asm (8 l.) -- tiny entry stub jmp _kmain, to guarantee the
    link-order-independent first-instruction-of-.text is a jump to the C entry.

  - boot_stage2.asm: after protected mode is entered, a dword-sized copy loop
    relocates the kernel from 0x21000 to 0x100000 (1 MiB). The final far-jump
    target becomes 0x00100000.

  - make_iso.sh: now links kernelAsm.o + kernel32.o, text base 0x100000, nasm -f
    win32 for the .o.

  - myboot.asm: trims kernel load range cap from 0xA000 to 0x9000 (now ends at
    0x9FFFF).

Context (guess -- no body):

  moves the kernel to its canonical 1 MiB address (where Linux and most x86
  kernels live), centralizes the C entry through an ASM trampoline, and
  introduces the first console helpers (cursor, newline handling, itoa) that
  later grow into a real tty subsystem.

## a886c6cd -- saving the new makefile

Commit: a886c6cd0a72b5e67106b34ad6a9a6eb3351f1aa
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 13 13:28:54 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - Makefile: big refactor.

  - Zero-fills a fresh os2.img (dd if=/dev/zero ... count=2880, i.e. a 1.44 MB
    floppy) during $(BUILD_DIR) target.

  - Combines boot_stage1 and boot_stage2 into a single
    $(BUILD_DIR)/bootloader.bin via cp + dd seek=1.

  - Kernel is written to os2.img at seek=8 (was 9) -- reflecting that the two
    bootloader stages now occupy 8 sectors exactly.

  - bootloader/boot_stage2.asm: kernel source address for the 1 MB copy loop
    moves from 0x21000 to 0x20E00 (offset chosen so stage2 padding fits in 4 KB
    - 512 B). Total stage2 image trimmed to 3584 bytes of actual code + 512-byte
    pad so stage1+stage2 = exactly 4 KB. Strips the commented-out idtr setup
    (already dead code).

## b7b7f6d7 -- handling faults and IRQs

Commit: b7b7f6d76ed62c306773fe8706eeb9b921db4d03
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 13 15:17:49 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  first real CPU-exception and PIC infrastructure. 917 new lines across 7 files.

  - New idt.c (237 l.) -- struct idt_entry, idt[256] array, idt_set_gate(),
    isrs_install() wiring ISR 0--31 with selector 0x08 / flags 0x8E (present,
    ring 0, 32-bit interrupt gate), string table exception_messages[32], and
    fault_handler(struct regs*) that writes the exception number and error code
    to screen via write_string()+itoa() then halt()s. Header comment credits
    "Bran's Kernel Development Tutorial".

  - New irq.c (128 l.) -- mirrors IDT setup for IRQs 32--47, irq_routines[16]
    table of custom handlers, irq_remap() reprograms master/slave 8259s to
    0x20/0x28, irq_handler() dispatches and sends EOI(s).

  - New include/commonDefs.h (66 l.) -- first "common" header:
    uint8_t/uint16_t/size_t typedefs, struct regs (segs, pusha set,
    int_no/err_code, CPU-pushed EIP/CS/EFLAGS/ESP/SS), inline
    outb/inb/halt/sti/magic_debug_break, and MSVC/Intellisense-friendly
    asmVolatile macro (for IDE parsing; actual builds still use GCC).

  - include/stringUtil.h -- now declares memset and #includes commonDefs.h.

  - kernelAsm.asm -- +464 lines: isr0..isr31 stubs (each cli; push err; push
    num; jmp isr_common_stub), irq0..irq15 stubs, _idt_load via lidt [_idtp].

  - kernel32.c -- strips inline outb/inb (now in commonDefs.h), calls
    idt_install() / irq_install() / sti() in kmain(), loops instead of halting.

  - stringUtil.c -- gains memset() impl (+6 l).

Context (guess -- no body):

  wiring the minimum needed for hardware interrupts -- CPU exceptions routed to
  a diagnostic printer, and IRQs routed through a dispatch table so future
  drivers can plug in handlers. The choice of code and comment style traces back
  to [Bran's OS-dev tutorial](http://www.osdever.net/bkerndev/index.php), which
  was a common starting point for osdev hobbyists in that era.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 90049678 -- the problem is related with the linking. Work-around with the
   bigfile idea

Commit: 90049678cf...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 13 22:58:56 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  Makefile introduces a "bigobject" build -- cat *.c > bigfile.c then compile
  that one translation unit into $(BUILD_DIR)/bigobject.o, linked with
  kernelAsm.o. Per-file %.o : %.c rule is commented out. Disables dep generation
  (DEPFLAGS =).

Context (subject):

  the per-file linking produced a binary where .data/.bss wasn't laid out the
  way the copy-to-1MB bootloader code assumed. Concatenating all C into one TU
  side-steps it while the real cause is investigated.

## 2f8d7035 -- adding an option to avoid zero-init vars in bss

Commit: 2f8d703529...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 14 01:23:32 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - Makefile -- adds -fno-zero-initialized-in-bss to CFLAGS. GCC normally puts
    zero-initialized globals in .bss; this flag forces them into .data instead
    so they get copied along with the rest of the loaded image (the bootloader's
    current objcopy -j .text -j .rdata -j .data flow drops .bss).

  - kernel32.c (+26 / -9) -- likely small cleanups related to globals now safely
    initialized.

Context (subject):

  the real fix for the "data corruption" chased over the last 3 commits. The
  kernel image doesn't yet allocate and zero .bss at runtime, so any int
  global_x; was reading uninitialized floppy bytes -- this flag works around
  that by turning .bss globals into .data entries with explicit zero
  initialization.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

    backed by itoa/uitoa and term_write_char.

  - idt.c, irq.c, term.c, kernel32.c -- existing write_string(...)+itoa(...)
    call sites collapse into single printk("...", ...) calls.

Context (subject):

  a real formatted-output primitive replaces the ad-hoc string+itoa pattern that
  had been proliferating across the kernel. First of many printk rewrites.

## 26bccde8 -- interface of syscalls works

Commit: 26bccde8a6...

## 73febeac -- implementing user-mode + sys call to kernel, and it works.

Commit: 73febeac88...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Apr 5 02:36:11 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - gdt.c (+120): the GDT table grows from 3 to 6 entries and gains a TSS. New
    entries: #3 user-mode code segment (0xFA/0xCF = ring 3 code), #4 user-mode
    data segment (0xF2/0xCF = ring 3 data), #5 TSS. New tss_entry_t and
    tss_entry global; write_tss(num, ss0, esp0) sets tss_entry.ss0 + esp0 (the
    kernel stack loaded on ring 3 -> ring 0 transitions);
    set_kernel_stack(uint32_t) updates esp0 dynamically. Calls gdt_load() then
    tss_flush() (LTR 0x2B) at install time.

  - idt.c -- IDT entries flagged to be accessible from user code (likely DPL 3
    on 0x80).

  - kernel32.c (+45): first code that will be switched to when ireting into ring
    3.

  - kernelAsm.asm -- adds _tss_flush (ltr ax).

Context (subject):

  milestone -- the kernel now has everything needed to jump down to ring 3
  (user-mode code/data segments, a working TSS). The follow-up commit 7dcbda17
  adds the actual iret trampoline.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 7dcbda17 -- fixing the problem with return from int80

Commit: 7dcbda17c9...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Apr 16 20:26:07 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernelAsm.asm -- new _switch_to_usermode_asm (+21 l.): loads DS/ES/FS/GS =
    0x23 (user data selector with RPL=3), pushes a fake interrupt frame (SS=0x23
    / ESP=0x2FFFFF / EFLAGS / CS=0x1B / EIP=_usermode_init) and irets --
    synthesizing an IRET from a ring-0 perspective so the CPU does the ring-3
    transition. Dedicated user stack at 0x2FFFFF.

  - commonDefs.h (-12) and kernel32.c (-30) -- strips dead/debug helpers
    superseded by the new ASM routine.

Context (subject):

  earlier int $0x80 had trouble returning cleanly to user mode (the IRET frame
  wasn't quite right). This commit is the proper "manual ring-switch" entry that
  gets the kernel's first usermode program running.

## 4be61399 -- implementing return from syscalls

Commit: 4be61399d5...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Apr 17 01:49:48 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - syscalls.c (+50 / -26): syscall fns now return int32_t and take proper C
    argument types (e.g. int32_t sys_write(int fd, const void *buf, size_t
    count), sys_open(const char*, int32_t, int32_t)); handle_syscall() extracts
    ebx/ecx/edx/esi/edi from the regs frame and passes them positionally. Return
    value is written back to r->eax so IRET delivers it as the syscall return.

  - kernelAsm.asm (+9 / -11): isr_common_stub now writes eax back to its slot in
    the pushed regs struct before popa, so the return value survives.

  - idt.c, kernel32.c, Makefile -- small adjustments.

## 5da316e0 -- fixing the bootloader

Commit: 5da316e0d4...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Apr 24 17:40:55 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - bootloader/boot_stage1.asm (+36 / -23): symbol renames for clarity
    (BASE_LOAD_ADDR -> BASE_LOAD_SEG, DEST_SEGMENT_KERNEL -> DEST_DATA_SEGMENT,
    counter -> currSectorNum, currSegmentKernel -> currDataSeg).
    SECTORS_TO_READ_AT_TIME drops from 8 to 1 -- one sector per int 13h call,
    simpler and more robust. Stack setup reworked: sp = 0x1FFF (8 KB stack above
    load address instead of 4K). The offset computation for destination in ES:BX
    drops the sub bx, 512 because currSectorNum now counts from 1 and the first
    increment happens before the first subtract.

  - bootloader/boot_stage2.asm (+10 / -9): minor matching tweaks.

  - init_src/asmInit.asm (+2 / -3): trivial.

Context (subject):

  stage1 had accumulated off-by-one issues (buffer offsets after rename/reorg)
  and was reading too many sectors at once, risking crossing DMA segment
  boundaries. The sector-at-a-time rewrite is both simpler and safer on real
  hardware.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 87f4d31f -- Implementing in a simple way the phyical page allocator

Commit: 87f4d31fb5...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun May 1 17:15:17 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New src/pageAllocator.c (82 l.) -- first-ever memory allocator in the
    kernel. Manages 128 MiB of physical RAM via a bitmap (pages_bit_field[8 *
    128] of uint32_t, 1 bit per 4 KiB page, 32 pages = 128 KiB per word).
    Exposes init_physical_page_allocator() (pre-marks the first 2 MiB used --
    kernel + stack), alloc_phys_page() (scans from last_index with wraparound,
    finds first zero bit via get_first_zero_bit_index), and free_phys_page(addr)
    (clears the bit and repoints last_index at the freshly-freed region for
    locality).

  - New include/kmalloc.h (10 l.) -- declares the three functions above.

  - kernel32.c (+22) -- calls init_physical_page_allocator() from kmain().

  - VS2015/myKernel.vcxproj deleted (160 l.) -- VS Intellisense project no
    longer maintained.

Context (subject):

  foundation for higher-level allocation. No paging, no virtual memory yet --
  just physical page accounting. This is the seed of what eventually becomes
  kernel/mm/.

## 7835a7b9 -- replacing in the bootloader slow copies with rep movsw/movsd

Commit: 7835a7b95a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon May 2 11:35:25 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  bootloader/boot_stage2.asm (+9 / -32):

  - The 1 KB real-mode copy of complete_flush -> 0x0000:0x1000 becomes a single
    rep movsw (CX=512 words instead of a 1024-byte manual loop).

  - The protected-mode copy of the kernel from 0x20E00 -> 0x100000 becomes a
    single rep movsd (ECX=131072 dwords = 512 KiB) instead of a manual
    dword-by-dword loop.

  - boot_stage1.asm -- 1 line trivial tweak.

Context (subject):

  rep-string instructions are microcoded to be both faster and smaller than
  explicit loops -- bootloader space savings + boot speed.

## fbb476ec -- the problem was related with the two 4KB buffers in paging.c.
   Replacing them with dynamic allocation. Switch to usermode with paging works.

Commit: fbb476ecef...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri May 6 23:08:24 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  src/paging.c (+17 / -17) -- the statically-allocated kernel_page_dir and
  kernel_page_table globals (__attribute__((aligned(4096)))) were colliding with
  the init binary's load region (both sat in memory that the bootloader had
  already filled with userspace code). The fix replaces them with
  alloc_phys_page() calls at init time -- the physical page allocator picks
  fresh free pages, avoiding the collision. src/pageAllocator.c / src/kernel32.c
  -- tiny adjustments.

Context (subject):

  root cause for the regression found. Static globals in .bss/.data at
  predictable addresses conflicted with the fixed 0x108000 init-app address;
  dynamic allocation side-steps it.

## 712f187a -- fixing the WRONG impl. of memmove() and other stuff

Commit: 712f187aec...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat May 7 19:53:58 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - include/stringUtil.h (+12 / -27) -- removes the broken inline memmove() that
    was actually just memcpy with volatile (didn't handle overlap at all).
    Declares memcpy / memmove as out-of-line. memset signature simplified (value
    is uint8_t).

  - src/stringUtil.c (+32) -- new inline-asm implementations:

  - memcpy: rep movsb for n % 4 bytes, then rep movsd for n / 4 dwords.

  - memmove: proper direction-aware copy (DF=1 + end pointers when dest > src).

  - src/term.c (+8 / -4), src/paging.c (+12 / -7): callers updated for the new
    signatures.

  - include/commonDefs.h (1 l.), include/paging.h (3 l.), Makefile (1 l.),
    src/kernel32.c (-3): minor.

Context (subject):

  memmove was silently aliasing memcpy. Scroll operations in term.c (which copy
  overlapping regions of the framebuffer/shadow buffer) would corrupt output
  when source and dest overlapped going the wrong direction. This is the first
  correct implementation.

## a85122ea -- relocating the kernel to 0xC010000 works. Just the switch to user
   mode doesn't now because the pages are priviledged

Commit: a85122ea99...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun May 8 13:40:29 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  higher-half kernel milestone.

  - src/link2.ld -- base address flips from 0x00100000 (1 MiB physical) to
    0xC0100000 (3 GiB + 1 MiB virtual). The kernel is now linked as if it lived
    at the top of the address space, mirroring Linux's i386 layout.

  - src/kernelAsm.asm (+54) -- _start now:

      1. Builds a minimal page directory at physical 0x1000 and a first page
         table at 0x2000 identity-mapping the low 4 MiB.

      2. Writes the same page-table pointer into both the directory entry for
         address 0 (index 0) and for address 0xC0000000 (index 768) -- so the
         low 4 MiB are accessible at both virtual addresses.

      3. Loads CR3 = 0x1000, sets CR0.PG, then jmp far eax with eax = 0xC0100400
         -- the "magic jump" to the high virtual address, after which EIP runs
         through the high-half mapping. Dead-reckons 1024-byte padding so the
         second jmp _kmain sits at offset 0x400 (0xC0100400).

  - src/kernel32.c / src/term.c -- small pointer adjustments; the VGA
    framebuffer at 0xB8000 still accessed identity-mapped for now.

Context (subject):

  kernel code now lives in the high 1 GiB of every process's virtual address
  space. The user-mode switch breaks because the newly-mapped pages haven't been
  flagged us=1 (user-accessible) -- follow-up commits fix page privileges.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 2f083370 -- fixing stack unalignment and syscall handling

Commit: 2f083370c5...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue May 17 21:31:42 2016 +0300

AI notes:

  cleans up argument passing). bootloader/boot_stage1.asm / boot_stage2.asm /
  src/kernel32.c -- tiny aligning tweaks (user stack pointer to 16-byte

  16B-aligned stack at function entry, and the earlier mov eax, 0x2FFFFF was an

================================================================================
  ERA 2 -- Native Linux + ELF  (Aug 2016 - Dec 2016)
================================================================================

  After a ~3.5 month gap (author's timezone briefly flips to US Pacific
  and back, suggesting a work-related relocation), development moves off
  Cygwin to native Linux hosts. Symbol prefix flips from _foo to foo;
  object files become real ELF; nasm -f elf32 replaces -f win32; the
  hand-rolled linker script is replaced with ld -m elf_i386 -Ttext. A
  pei-i386 linker-script fossil is kept briefly as reference, then
  deleted. The era's technical agenda: stacktrace + panic + assert, a
  first pass at unit tests (host-side printf executable), the full
  buddy-based kmalloc allocator bring-up (an arc spanning 30+ commits
  in Nov 2016), physical-page-allocator pool split for paging
  reservations, copy-on-write fork with page-refcounting, the first
  scheduler, kernel threads, process exit, and the Linux-style list.h
  macro library. By the end of this era, the kernel tree reorganizes
  from src/ to kernel/ + kernel/include/ and adopts snake_case
  filenames -- but the build is still one Makefile per subdirectory.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 4e8c99d6 -- making the kernel buildable only under a 32-bit linux

## 5e4a8470 -- fixed a terrible bug in paging

Commit: 5e4a847053...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Aug 27 23:52:30 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  src/paging.c (+45 / -2) -- fix for a latent bug: map_page() was storing the
  newly-allocated page-table's physical address directly into
  pdir->page_tables[i], then dereferencing that pointer to zero-init the table.
  With paging on, dereferencing a raw physical address goes through translation
  and lands on unrelated memory. The fix: keep pdir->entries[i].pageTableAddr as
  the physical addr (correct -- that's what the MMU reads), but translate the
  pointer through KERNEL_PADDR_TO_VADDR(ptable) before storing it in
  page_tables[i] (used by C code) and before calling
  initialize_empty_page_table(). New debug helpers debug_count_used_pdir_entries
  / debug_dump_used_pdir_entries for sanity-checking. init_src/init.c gains
  printf("&stackVar = %p\n", &stackVar); -- proving userspace actually sees its
  own stack address.

Context (subject):

  worth reading. This is the archetypal virt/phys confusion bug in higher-half
  paging. It would have corrupted memory on every page-table allocation once the
  kernel had been re-mapped.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## b80c79b0 -- removing the phy. addr member from the page_directory_t

What changed:

  src/paging.c (1 l.), src/kernel32.c (-1), init_src/Makefile (1 l.),
  init_src/usermode_syscall_wrappers.h (1 l.) -- flips the kernel page-table
  entries' us bit from 1 to 0 (supervisor-only). Previously kernel pages were
  incorrectly marked user-accessible, which would let userland read kernel
  memory. Now properly enforced.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 7f7b27d6 -- Adding stacktrace dump utility to the kernel and making panic to
   use it

Commit: 7f7b27d602...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Aug 28 18:56:12 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New src/debug_utils.c (62 l.) + include/debug_utils.h (12 l.).
    stackwalk32(frames, count) walks the EBP chain via ebp = *(void)ebp; retAddr
    = *((void)ebp + 1); up to count frames. dump_stacktrace() walks 10 frames
    and printks each frame's return address. The two
    debug_count_used_pdir_entries / debug_dump_used_pdir_entries helpers
    relocate here from paging.c.

  - src/kernel32.c -- panic() now calls dump_stacktrace() before halting.

  - src/paging.c loses 21 lines (the moved debug helpers).

  - Makefile -- top-level: -fno-omit-frame-pointer added to CFLAGS (required for
    the EBP walk). include/paging.h (-5).

Context (guess -- no body):

  critical infrastructure -- any ASSERT or panic now prints where in the kernel
  it fired, making crashes actually debuggable without a debugger attached.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 3bd70023 -- moving init to 0x08000000, improving the page fault handling and
   enabling the WP bit to have write protect in supervisor mode

Commit: 3bd7002396...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Aug 28 22:46:56 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  - init_src/Makefile -- init binary load address 0x108000/0xC0120000 ->
    0x08000000 (128 MiB virtual). Init no longer lives in the high-half kernel
    space.

  - src/kernelAsm.asm (+2 / -1) -- after setting CR0.PG, also or eax, 0x10000 to
    enable CR0.WP (write-protect). Without WP, ring-0 code could write to
    read-only pages regardless of the RW bit; WP makes the RW bit enforced even
    in supervisor mode -- catches bad kernel writes to rodata.

  - src/paging.c (+13 / -1) -- handle_page_fault() now reads CR2 (faulting
    address) and the error-code bits (present/rw/us) and prints a structured
    diagnostic: "*** PAGE FAULT in attempt to {READ|WRITE} <cr2> from
    {kernel|userland} (NON present page)" before ASSERT. Much more useful than
    the old one-liner.

  - src/kernel32.c (+12 / -10) -- adjusts for the init binary's new virtual
    address.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 5588c8e1 -- minor changes avoiding page fault in page fault

Commit: 5588c8e139...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Aug 28 23:11:17 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  src/paging.c (+9) checks that CR2/pdir lookups are valid before dereferencing
  from the page-fault handler; src/debug_utils.c (+34) -- stackwalk32 now
  bounds-checks the frame pointer against the kernel stack range before deref;
  include/debug_utils.h (+3), include/commonDefs.h (+4 / -4).

Context (subject):

  classic double-fault prevention -- a page fault handler that itself takes a
  page fault leads to triple-fault / reset. Makes both the handler and the stack
  walker robust to corrupted state.

## 92334165 -- working on paging..

Commit: 92334165c8...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Oct 16 13:52:18 2016 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  src/paging.c (+112 / -12) -- major expansion of the paging API:

  - is_mapped(pdir, vaddr) -- returns whether a virtual address is currently
    mapped.

  - unmap_page(pdir, vaddr) -- returns whether it unmapped anything (clears the
    page_t entry).

  - map_pages(pdir, vaddr, paddr, count, us, rw) -- loops map_page over a range.

  - kbasic_virtual_alloc(pdir, vaddr, size, us, rw) -- allocates size bytes
    worth of new physical pages and maps them at vaddr.

  - kbasic_virtual_free(pdir, vaddr, size) -- inverse.

  - map_page() now ASSERTs that both vaddr and paddr are 4K-aligned; debug
    printks simplified.

  - include/paging.h (+14) -- declares all the above.

  - src/debug_utils.c (+29) -- more paging diagnostics.

  - src/kernel32.c (-42) -- removes hand-rolled map/unmap code now subsumed by
    the new API.

Context (subject):

  foundation for real kernel VA management. kbasic_virtual_alloc/free are the
  primitives that a future kmalloc will sit on top of.

## f566adcf -- adding static_assert and making regs a typedef

Commit: f566adcf90...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Nov 5 16:43:40 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  include/commonDefs.h gets a portable compile-time assertion and starts
  treating pointer-size integers abstractly, with arch-guarded checks.

  - static_assert(expr) macro -- expands to _Static_assert(expr, "Static
    assertion failed") on GCC, and to nothing under MSVC's Intellisense
    parser.

  - uintptr_t / intptr_t / ptrdiff_t -- redefined from fixed uint32_t /
    int32_t to size_t / ssize_t, so they track pointer size.

  - Sanity checks at file scope: static_assert(sizeof(uintptr_t) ==
    sizeof(intptr_t)), sizeof(uintptr_t) == sizeof(void *), plus
    arch-guarded sizeof(void *) == 4 on __i386__ and == 8 on __x86_64__.

  - struct regs promoted to a typedef regs (callers in idt.c, irq.c,
    syscalls.c, paging.c, kernel32.c drop the "struct" keyword).

Context (guess -- no body):

  First step toward supporting a 64-bit build. Even though no x86_64 code
  exists yet, the types and checks are in place so later commits can flip
  architectures without reshuffling every declaration.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 639ff585 -- Starting to isolate i386-specific code

Commit: 639ff585af...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Nov 5 17:08:50 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  First carve-out of an arch-specific header tree.

  - New include/arch/i386/paging_int.h (56 l.) -- holds the i386-specific
    page_t / page_table_t / page_dir_entry_t bitfield structs plus the
    page_directory_t struct definition, all the 4 KiB-page 32-bit layout
    bits that shouldn't leak into arch-independent code.

  - include/paging.h (-57) -- loses the concrete struct layouts; now only
    forward-declares struct page_directory_t and keeps the prototypes
    (map_page, init_paging, is_mapped, unmap_page, kbasic_virtual_alloc,
    kbasic_virtual_free, etc.).

  - include/commonDefs.h -- adds #error Platform not supported for unknown
    __i386__ / __x86_64__ fallthrough.

  - src/paging.c (+6 / -16), src/debug_utils.c (+5) -- include the new
    arch header where the concrete struct is needed.

Context (subject says it):

  Kicks off the kernel/arch/ vs kernel/ split that becomes a pervasive
  organizational pattern. The pair (arch-independent API header +
  arch-specific internal header) is still used today across the tree.

## 0141cdda -- starting to write the data structures for the allocator

Commit: 0141cddafe...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Nov 10 23:12:58 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  src/kmalloc.c -- carves out the allocator's data model.

  - #defines MIN_BLOCK_SIZE = 32, BIG_CHUNK_SIZE = 1 MiB, BIG_CHUNK_COUNT =
    128 (so a 128 MiB heap); derived constants
    BLOCK_NODES_IN_META_DATA_OBJ = 2 * BIG_CHUNK_SIZE / MIN_BLOCK_SIZE,
    CHUNKS_IN_METADATA_CHUNK.

  - static_assert()s that MIN_BLOCK_SIZE is 16/32/64 and BIG_CHUNK_SIZE is
    a multiple of 1 MiB.

  - typedef struct block_node { split:1; free:1; unused:6; } -- one-byte
    per-node metadata.

  - typedef chunk_meta_data_obj wrapping nodes[BLOCK_NODES_IN_META_DATA_OBJ].

  - typedef meta_data_chunk wrapping 16 meta_data_objects, sized to fill a
    BIG_CHUNK exactly -- so every 16th 1 MiB chunk is reserved for
    metadata covering the next 15 data chunks.

  - get_free_chunk_index() skips the metadata chunks (indices divisible by
    CHUNKS_IN_METADATA_CHUNK) when scanning full_chunks_table.

  - full_chunks_table / initialized_slots renamed for clarity.

  src/pageAllocator.c, unittests/tests_main.cpp -- trivial.

Context (guess -- subject):

  Lays out a buddy-allocator-style meta-data layout in the kernel heap.
  A binary tree of block_nodes tracks which sub-blocks are free/split. The
  splitting of the heap into 1 MiB "big chunks", each with its own nodes
  tree, keeps the metadata compact and the recursion shallow.

## cd46e5ca -- partially implemented the allocator. Nothing was tested

Commit: cd46e5ca1e...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Nov 11 13:52:12 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  First real kmalloc() body: a buddy-style recursive allocator over a
  single flat 512 MiB heap.

  - src/kmalloc.c (+105 / -58) -- design changes from the previous
    commit's chunk-based layout to a single contiguous region:
    HEAP_DATA_SIZE = 512 MiB, BLOCK_NODES_IN_META_DATA = 2 *
    HEAP_DATA_SIZE / MIN_BLOCK_SIZE, HEAP_DATA_ADDR = HEAP_BASE_ADDR +
    metadata size. block_node gains a data_allocated : 1 bit.

  - New allocate_node_rec(size, node_size, node, vaddr) -- recursive
    descent of the implicit binary tree via NODE_LEFT /NODE_RIGHT /
    NODE_PARENT macros (standard heap array indexing). Lazily
    kbasic_virtual_alloc()s the metadata page for a node on first touch
    (if (node & (PAGE_SIZE - 1)) == 0 heuristic). Splits a free node,
    recurses left; if left fails, recurses right.

  - allocate_node(size) -- entry-point wrapper; clamps size to
    MIN_BLOCK_SIZE.

  - Also drops the per-chunk accounting tables
    (full_chunks_table/initialized_slots) in favor of the single tree.

  - include/kmalloc.h (+1) / src/main.c (1 l.) -- signature tweak.

  - unittests/tests_main.cpp (+20) -- first test calling kmalloc() on the
    new implementation.

  - unittests/Makefile (+3) -- a link flag or source-glob adjustment.

Context (subject):

  The allocator is a classic buddy system laid over the metadata tree.
  Subject warns that nothing's been tested yet -- the next commits add
  tests and fixes.

## 1ad88e96 -- improving kmalloc() by making it non-recursive and other
   benchmark stuff

Commit: 1ad88e9699...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Nov 12 22:05:53 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - src/kmalloc.c (+163 / -143) -- reshape of the core allocator.

      1. allocate_node_rec() is replaced by an iterative walk that visits
         the implicit-tree left-first with a manual "come back up to the
         right subtree" step using NODE_IS_LEFT() and NODE_PARENT(). No
         more recursion depth dependent on heap height (~24 for 512 MiB).
      2. log2(n) renamed to log2_for_power_of_2(n) (CPU-level log2 via
         BSR; fast path for exact powers of two that the allocator uses
         for sizes).
      3. Helpers like node_has_page() moved above allocate_node()
         callers and marked static ALWAYS_INLINE.
      4. set_no_free_uplevels() / set_free_uplevels() marked static.

  - include/commonDefs.h (+46) -- likely adds helpers used by the new
    walker (ALIGN_UP, NODE_* macros, or BSR-based log2).

  - include/kmalloc.h (+4 / -2) -- signature tweaks.

  - src/kmalloc_util.c (+8 / -1), src/main.c (-1) -- small.

  - unittests/tests_main.cpp (+30 / -27) -- benchmark harness compares
    old vs new allocate latency.

Context (subject):

  The recursion could be ~24 deep on a 512 MiB heap, costing each
  call a fresh stack frame. The iterative version trims latency and
  makes the allocator's worst-case stack usage constant.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 521fb730 -- considerably improving kmalloc() by avoiding calls to
   is_mapped()

Commit: 521fb7307c...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Nov 13 12:34:15 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  src/kmalloc.c (+48 / -36) -- removes the per-allocation call to
  is_mapped() (which walks page-directory/page-table every time) in the
  hot path. Introduces a new file-scope bitmap
  allocation_for_metadata_nodes[] where each byte covers 8 pages = 32 KiB
  of heap nodes. node_has_page(node) just indexes into the bitmap with
  (node * sizeof(block_node)) >> 15 -- O(1) instead of a page-table walk.
  evenually_allocate_page_for_node() sets the bit on first allocation.

Context (guess -- subject):

  The benchmark harness added two commits earlier surfaced is_mapped() as
  the dominant cost; this is the resulting optimization. Also changes the
  strategy: allocate 8 pages at once (32 KiB) rather than 1 page per
  metadata demand, amortizing the kbasic_virtual_alloc() cost.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## d50a4aab -- fixing nasty bugs in the free logic

Commit: d50a4aab51...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Nov 15 18:53:04 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - src/kmalloc.c (+46 / -13) -- several bugs in kfree:

      1. New is_block_node_free(block_node n) predicate defined as
         n.free && !n.split. set_free_uplevels() now uses it on both
         children, so a split child never looks "free enough to
         coalesce" (that was the chaos-test bug).
      2. kfree() asserts that the released node isn't split (catches
         size-argument mismatches that previously silently corrupted
         the tree).
      3. set_free_uplevels now returns early with curr_size halved
         when it can't coalesce, so callers know exactly how big the
         merged block ended up. That's the unit used to decide
         page-return.

  - unittests/tests_main.cpp (+4 / -3), unittests/mocks.c (1 l.) -- test
    adjustments + keeping the mocks in sync with the tightened asserts.

## 1a6146b3 -- making possible a small block to free pages for
   bigger-than-page-size blocks

Commit: 1a6146b34e...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Nov 15 20:42:05 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - src/kmalloc.c (+36 / -23) -- set_free_uplevels() gets an out-param
    *node pointing at the highest node successfully coalesced. kfree()
    uses that to locate the outermost freed block and, when that block
    spans >= PAGE_SIZE, returns the underlying physical pages.
    Previously a kfree() of a small block that completed a larger
    free buddy could leave the backing pages mapped; now the physical
    pages are returned whenever the coalesced region crosses page
    boundaries.

  - include/commonDefs.h (1 l.), unittests/tests_main.cpp (+17 / -3)
    -- tests exercise kmalloc(8 KB)/kfree + kmalloc(small)/... sequences
    that trigger the page-return path.

Context (subject):

  Closes the last correctness gap: coalescing correctly propagates page
  ownership back to the page allocator even when the user freed a small
  block that happened to complete a multi-page buddy.

  "coalesced region is large, so try to return pages" logic is gated
  behind curr_size >= PAGE_SIZE rather than aggressively running for
  every kfree. Subject explains the reasoning: a small block's kfree
  typically only merges up to something still sub-page, so scanning for
  returnable pages on every small free was wasted work.

  unittests/tests_main.cpp (1 l.) -- tiny.

## 4cc69082 -- introducing a realistic perf test in the kernel after fixing
   some problems with paging

Commit: 4cc6908266...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Nov 17 14:47:49 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - src/pageAllocator.c (+92 / -13) -- splits the physical page
    allocator into a **general** pool and a **paging-reserved** pool so
    map_page() can always allocate a fresh page table without competing
    with kmalloc()'s backing-page needs.

      * #defines INITIAL_MB_RESERVED = 2 (kernel code/data),
        MB_RESERVED_FOR_PAGING = 1, USABLE_MEM_SIZE_IN_MB = 128 - 3.
      * paging_alloc_phys_page() / paging_free_phys_page() -- draw
        only from the reserved pool.
      * alloc_phys_page() -- draws only from the USABLE pool,
        skipping both reserved regions.
      * The unconditional "mark first 2 MiB used" block is commented
        out (the pool split makes it redundant).

  - src/i386/paging.c (+11 / -7) -- map_page() now calls
    paging_alloc_phys_page() for the page tables themselves.

  - src/kmalloc.c (+17 / -2), include/kmalloc.h (+2 / -2) -- plumbing
    for the updated page-alloc API.

  - New src/perftests_data.c (103 l.) -- canned data tables for a
    realistic allocation workload (sizes + operation sequences taken
    from real code profiles).

  - src/perftests.c (+70) -- kmalloc_realistic_perf_test() drives that
    workload and RDTSCs throughput.

  - unittests/tests_main.cpp (+6 / -2) / Makefile (+4 / -4) / src/main.c
    (+2 / -2) -- wire up the new perf test.

Context (subject):

  The chaotic trivial perf test didn't hit the realistic access patterns
  where paging allocations and user allocations compete. The pool split
  ensures map_page() can't OOM because kmalloc consumed all pages; the
  data-driven perf test exercises that scenario.

## fdb6e978 -- adding int64 support on the 32-bit kernel and making RDTSC to
   work correctly

Commit: fdb6e97897...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Nov 18 20:42:42 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New src/i386/int64ops.s (842 l.) -- full set of soft-float-style
    64-bit arithmetic helpers for i386 (signed/unsigned multiplication,
    division, modulo, shift). These are the libgcc routines pasted in
    so the kernel doesn't have to link against libgcc for `long long`
    operations.

  - include/commonDefs.h -- RDTSC() now returns uint64_t. On BITS64 it
    combines edx:eax; on BITS32 it uses the "=A" constraint to pull
    edx:eax into a single 64-bit destination.

  - src/stringUtil.c (+160 / -40) -- renames / adds: itoa() stays
    intptr_t; new llitoa(int64_t) / llutoa(uint64_t) for long-long
    values; printk/vprintk gain a "%lld" / "%llu" path.

  - src/perftests.c (+6 / -8) -- switches timing to uint64_t now that
    RDTSC returns the full counter.

  - Makefile (1 l.), src/i386/Makefile (+6 / -2) -- nasm -f elf32 for
    the new .s file.

Context (subject):

  RDTSC returns a 64-bit counter; the previous i386 path only kept the
  low 32 bits, which wrapped around every ~3 seconds at 1 GHz. True
  64-bit arithmetic in the kernel means llong multiplies and shifts
  also work -- needed once the benchmark results get bigger than
  2^32 cycles.

## 509dd069 -- Improving kmalloc (#8)

Commit: 509dd06947...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Nov 19 13:31:04 2016 +0200

Message:

  Improving the performance of kmalloc() by switching from a PAGE_SIZE
  block alloc size to a generic ALLOC_BLOCK_SIZE, currently set to 8
  pages. That reduces the amount of mapping/unmapping of pages and
  allocation of physical pages as well.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - src/kmalloc.c (+42 / -38) -- #define ALLOC_BLOCK_SIZE (8 *
    PAGE_SIZE), STATIC_ASSERT it's a multiple of PAGE_SIZE. The
    "allocated" bit on block_node is now used at the ALLOC_BLOCK_SIZE
    tier (was PAGE_SIZE). When a kmalloc crosses into a fresh block,
    the allocator reserves an 8-page chunk up-front rather than
    mapping pages lazily one at a time. Halves map_page() calls for
    mid-sized allocations.

  - include/paging.h (+14 / -3) -- moves kernel_page_dir extern and
    get_curr_page_dir() / get_kernel_page_dir() accessors into
    inline-ALWAYS helpers in the header (removes two function calls
    per kmalloc).

  - src/i386/paging.c (+19 / -31) / src/kmalloc_util.c (+2 / -2) --
    strip the now-inlined accessors from their old locations.

  - src/perftests.c (-31), unittests/tests_main.cpp (+17 / -11),
    unittests/Makefile (-1) -- bench and test adjustments for the
    faster path.

  - include/commonDefs.h (-5) -- removes unused tier-old definitions.

Context (PR body is explicit):

  First merged pull request (#8), which is why the subject is unusual
  for this era. Marks the first time Tilck accepts contributions via
  the PR workflow rather than straight pushes.

## d943ab59 -- making the loader to load up to 1000 sectors to avoid a problem
   on real HW

Commit: d943ab5952...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Nov 20 23:45:13 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  bootloader/boot_stage1.asm (+31 / -35) -- caps the kernel-load loop at
  1000 sectors (was scanning the whole disk geometry). Some real BIOSes
  would error or time out when asked to read past the actual end of a
  small image; bounding the load count fixes it without changing what's
  actually read. run_qemu_hda -- file mode change only.

## 03681b8b -- Improving the 1st stage of the bootloader

Commit: 03681b8b03...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Nov 26 14:42:24 2016 +0200

Message:

  This change makes the 1st stage of the bootloader to relocate itself
  to 0x20000 and then to load the rest of its own body as the 2nd
  stage bootloader. This makes a lot of things simpler. (#11)

AI notes:

What changed:

  bootloader/boot.asm (+55 / -59) -- self-relocation pattern:

    1. Entry at BASE_LOAD_SEG (0x07C0) -- where BIOS drops MBR.
    2. Stage1 copies its own 512 bytes from 0x07C0:0 to the
       DEST_DATA_SEGMENT (0x2000:0) via rep movsw (256 words).
    3. Far-jumps to DEST_DATA_SEGMENT:after_reloc -- now running at the
       same address the kernel will later live at.
    4. From there, reads its own remaining sectors (stage2 body) via
       int 13h, directly behind itself in the target segment.
    5. The video-mode setup that used to sit at the top of start: is
       dropped (the merged stage2 handles it).

Context (PR body explains):

  Simplifies the geometry: "where stage1 runs" and "where stage2 loads"
  are now the same segment. Eliminates the far-jump and segment-swap
  dance that the earlier two-file layout required.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## de8b046a -- Working on processes (#12)

Commit: de8b046a52...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Dec 4 19:59:11 2016 +0200

Message:

  Introducing pdir_clone() and copy-on-write for userland.
  The next step will be to introduce fork() and a trivial scheduler.

AI notes:

What changed:

  First real work on processes. Adds the fundamentals that fork() will
  need: cloned page directories and copy-on-write.

  - New include/arch/i386/process_int.h (19 l.) -- struct process_info
    (next *, pid, tid, state, regs state_regs, page_directory_t *pdir).

  - New src/i386/process.c (17 l.) -- arch-specific half of processes.

  - src/process.c (-3) -- generic half loses its stub include.

  - include/arch/i386/paging_int.h (+8) -- page_directory_t gains a
    uintptr_t paddr field so set_page_directory() can load CR3
    directly without computing KERNEL_VADDR_TO_PADDR each time.

  - src/i386/paging.c (+124 / -34):

      * handle_page_fault() checks for the COW pattern (us=1, rw=1,
        p=1, and avail bits set to PAGE_COW_FLAG|PAGE_COW_ORIG_RW).
        On match, copies the page to a scratch buffer, allocates a
        fresh physical page, rewires the PTE to the new page with
        rw=1, copies the content back, and returns -- the write
        transparently succeeds without a real fault.
      * Adds pdir_clone() that walks the source page directory,
        allocates a new arch-level pdir, marks all writable user
        pages as read-only in both pdirs, and stores the COW avail
        bits so the fault handler can tell a COW page from an
        ordinary RO one. curr_page_dir now tracked separately from
        kernel_page_dir.

  - include/paging.h (+10 / -5), src/i386/gdt.c (+19 / -21),
    src/i386/kernelAsm.asm (+5 / -3), init_src/init.c (+16 / -7),
    src/main.c (+32 / -24), src/timer.c (+2 / -3) -- callers / init
    updates.

  - src/pageAllocator.c (1 l.), include/commonDefs.h (+4 / -4),
    include/process.h (+9) -- small plumbing.

  - Makefile (+4 / -4) -- builds the new i386/process.c.

Context (PR body is explicit):

  Copy-on-write is the critical primitive fork() needs to be
  efficient. This commit has the mechanism (fault handler + pdir
  clone); the next commits add fork() and scheduling on top.

## 7044ad95 -- Context switch (#14)

Commit: 7044ad9591...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Dec 11 22:12:20 2016 +0200

Message:

  Implementing the actual context switch function and discarding the
  older switch to user mode one. Now, even if there still no
  "processes", the schedule() function uses context_switch() to return
  to the process, instead of using the regular return code. This means
  that it will be enough to save 'regs' to a process entry in order to
  switch among many processes.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - src/i386/kernelAsm.asm (+40 / -18) -- switch_to_usermode_asm
    renamed to asm_context_switch_x86. Takes the full regs struct as
    stack-passed arguments (gs/fs/es/ds segments first, then the
    general-purpose set, then the CPU-pushed frame of eip/cs/eflags/
    useresp/ss). Restores all via pops then iret -- same IRET trick
    as before, but now general over ANY saved register state, not
    just "go to fresh usermode".

  - src/i386/process.c (+61) -- ALWAYS_INLINE static context_switch(regs
    *r) that marshals the regs fields into the argument stack for the
    asm call; first_usermode_switch() now builds a zero-initialized
    regs and calls context_switch(); schedule() replaces the special
    case for the timer with a generic PIC_sendEOI() + context_switch().

  - src/i386/paging.c (+3 / -3), src/main.c (+10 / -16),
    bootloader/boot.asm (+1), include/commonDefs.h (+4), include/irq.h
    (+1) -- callers and declarations.

Context (PR body is explicit):

  The old switch_to_usermode_asm could only go from "ring 0 now" to
  "ring 3 at a fresh entry point". The new asm_context_switch_x86
  can resume ANY pushed-regs snapshot, which is exactly what a
  scheduler needs. No processes yet, but the mechanism is in place.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 27eb9355 -- Working on fork (#15)

Commit: 27eb9355f8...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Dec 12 23:43:17 2016 +0200

Message:

  Finally implementing fork() and making it to work!! That's amazing!

AI notes:

What changed:

  - src/i386/process.c (+86 / -19) -- real process-list management and
    fork:

      * processes_list (circular doubly-linked), current_process,
        current_max_pid file-scope globals.
      * add_process(p) -- inserts at tail of the ring.
      * first_usermode_switch() -- now kmalloc()s a process_info,
        assigns pid = ++current_max_pid, memmoves regs in, adds to
        list, loads pdir, and context_switch()es to it.
      * save_current_process_state(regs *) -- copies the trapped
        register frame into the current process's state_regs (called
        from the generic IRQ/ISR path before the scheduler runs).
      * switch_to_process(pi) -- sets current_process, switches pdir
        if different, calls context_switch().
      * schedule() -- picks the next process in the ring.
      * fork_current_process() -- creates a new process_info,
        pdir_clones the current pdir, sets the child's return eax
        to 0 (so fork returns 0 in the child), adds to list, leaves
        the parent's eax pointing at the new pid.

  - include/process.h (+6 / -2) -- declares save_current_process_state
    / fork_current_process / first_usermode_switch (now takes pdir).

  - init_src/init.c (+19 / -3), init_src/usermode_syscall_wrappers.h
    (+9 / -4) -- userland test that calls fork() and prints which side
    of the return it got.

  - src/syscalls.c (+7) -- sys_fork() wires to fork_current_process().

  - src/timer.c (+5 / -2), src/main.c (-8), debug_run_qemu -- tiny.

Context (PR subject):

  The whole fork + COW chain from commit de8b046a lands here. The
  kernel now supports multiple user processes sharing the kernel.

================================================================================
  ERA 3 -- Real tooling  (Dec 2016 - Jan 2017)
================================================================================

  The project graduates from "toy kernel" to "project with conventions".
  First .gitignore, first build_toolchain.sh (apt-get install + clone
  googletest), first gtest suite (replacing the stand-alone printf
  testmain), first musl-libc + dietlibc in the toolchain, first real
  ELF loader in the kernel (kernel can now run arbitrary statically-
  linked ELF32 binaries), and init becomes a real ELF program compiled
  against dietlibc with proper argc/argv/envp on the stack. Still built
  with per-directory Makefiles, but the scaffolding for a real CI run
  is in place. A short era -- only a few weeks -- but structurally
  important: after this the codebase has tests, is portable across dev
  machines via the toolchain script, and can bootstrap a real userland
  program.

## 12a57f81 -- Rename stringUtil.h to string_util.h

What changed:

  Pure rename + include path update across 17 files:
  include/stringUtil.h -> include/string_util.h; each .c file switches
  its #include "stringUtil.h" to "string_util.h". Completes the
  CamelCase -> snake_case conversion for header names (the .c twin was
  renamed in b4a3714d / PR #16).

## 0d313234 -- fixing cow (#17)

Commit: 0d31323435...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Dec 17 14:30:13 2016 +0200

Message:

  Fixing the incorrect implementation of COW by using ref-count.
  Now, after fork() both parent and child have COW pages. Anyone who
  writes on a given page, copies it and decreases its ref-count, if
  its ref-count is > 1. In the case its ref-count is 1, that means
  that nobody else refers with COW on that page, so the page is used
  directly after marking as "regular".

AI notes:

What changed:

  - src/i386/paging.c (+110 / -52) -- big rewrite of COW handling:

      * New u16 *pageframes_refcount pointer, allocated at paging init
        to hold a 16-bit refcount per physical page.
      * handle_potential_cow(vaddr) extracted from handle_page_fault:
        reads refcount; if == 1, converts the PTE to a plain writable
        page in place; if > 1, allocates a fresh page, decrements the
        source page's refcount, copies the content, and rewires the
        PTE. Returns true/false so handle_page_fault can distinguish
        COW faults from real ones.
      * pdir_clone() now increments refcount on every shared page
        rather than only-marking-parent-as-COW.

  - src/pageframe_allocator.c (+6 / -1) -- exposes a refcount
    getter/setter pair for paging.c to touch.

  - include/paging.h (+20 / -11), include/commonDefs.h (+3),
    include/process.h (+1 / -1) -- declarations.

  - init_src/init.c (+3 / -1), src/main.c (+5 / -1),
    src/i386/process.c (+9 / -2), src/syscalls.c (+2 / -1) -- callers.

Context (PR body):

  The earlier COW was broken because after the fault the parent's
  page was left read-only even though it no longer needed to be.
  Refcounting lets the last-writer-wins path skip the copy
  altogether, which is the common case after fork+exec.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## c74f6125 -- using INVLPG correctly

Commit: c74f612544...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Dec 17 16:47:47 2016 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - src/i386/paging.c (+13 / -4) -- invalidate_tlb_page() was being
    called on the PAGE TABLE address (uptr)ptable instead of the actual
    page virtual address being modified. Fixed to invlpg the user
    vaddr whose PTE changed.

  - src/i386/process.c (+4 / -1) -- same fix in pdir_clone's COW
    setup.

  - include/commonDefs.h (+5 / -2) -- invalidate_tlb_page macro
    clarified.

Context (subject):

  Subtle x86 TLB semantics -- INVLPG takes the linear address whose
  translation to invalidate, not the physical page table that
  contains it. This was silently masked by most context switches
  (CR3 load flushes whole TLB); bugs only appeared when modifying
  PTEs within the same pdir.

## 96fa246c -- Introducing _exit() (#18)

Commit: 96fa246cf4...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Dec 18 21:02:32 2016 +0200

Message:

  * implementing process exit
  * fully implementing _exit(): now we have pdir_destroy() which frees
    all the pages owned by a given process
  * making the pageframe allocator to use uptr instead of void * params
  * some refactoring in paging
  * fixing 80-col limit for some files
  * fixing 80-col limit in all the code
  * some refactoring in the interrupt handling code, which includes a
    fix in the scheduler that now will still receive IRQs even if in
    halt() state.

AI notes:

What changed:

  Big PR (29 files, +527 / -370). Three substantive pieces:

  - Process exit: src/i386/process.c and src/syscalls.c gain exit()
    logic. New pdir_destroy(pdir) walks the page directory, releases
    every present physical page through the refcount-aware free path,
    and unmaps / frees the page tables themselves. src/i386/paging.c
    adds the walker. process_info tracks exit state so the scheduler
    can clean up after the context leaves.

  - 80-col enforcement: across all 26 source files, long lines are
    wrapped. No semantic change.

  - Interrupt-path refactor: src/i386/kernelAsm.asm (+54 / -75)
    simplifies the ISR/IRQ stubs -- a lot of the boilerplate was
    folded into macros. Scheduler tweak: halt() now loops on sti +
    hlt rather than plain hlt so timer IRQs can still preempt.

  Also: init_src/syscall_interface.h (68 l.) extracted -- user-side
  syscall number definitions moved out of usermode_syscall_wrappers.h
  (which was becoming a grab-bag). pageframe_allocator transitions
  from void* to uptr in its public API.

Context (PR body enumerates what landed):

  First process can now exit cleanly; pdir_destroy() correctly
  returns all physical pages. With fork() already working, this
  closes the fork-exec-exit loop at the primitive level (exec is
  still missing).

## e8532b1f -- Adding basic ELF support in the kernel (#20)

Commit: e8532b1f61...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Jan 7 15:09:08 2017 +0200

Message:

  * small steps for the elf loader
  * the elf loader works
  * minor fixes
  * fixing a nasty bug in the boot loader
  * making run_qemu_hda to be the default run_qemu script
  * making the elf loader to load bss and to distinguish between ro
    and rw segments
  * adding code that un-maps the temporary mapping of elf in kernel
    space

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New kernel/include/elf.h (2143 l.) -- the entire ELF
    specification: ELFCLASS32 / ELFCLASS64, Elf32_Ehdr / Elf32_Phdr /
    Elf32_Shdr / Elf32_Sym, relocation records, section flags,
    program header types, e_machine constants. Verbatim from the
    System V ABI spec so the loader can use the canonical names.

  - New kernel/elf_loader.c (144 l.) -- load_elf_program(elf, pdir,
    entry, stack_addr) walks Elf32_Phdrs, for each PT_LOAD segment:
    allocates pages_count pages = ceil((memsz + PAGE_SIZE) / PAGE_SIZE),
    copies p_filesz bytes from elf+p_offset, zero-fills up to p_memsz
    (bss), maps into pdir with us=1 and rw = (p_flags & PF_W). After
    all segments, unmaps the temporary kernel-side mapping of the ELF
    file.

  - kernel/i386/paging.c (+12 / -4), kernel/include/paging.h (+12):
    get_mapping() exposed to the loader. kernel/main.c (+32 / -8) --
    replaces the hand-built first-usermode-switch demo with a real
    load_elf_program() + first_usermode_switch() flow.

  - bootloader/boot.asm (+20 / -14) -- "nasty bug in the boot loader"
    fix: a sector-count off-by-one when the load count exceeded a
    track boundary. The bootloader now sees init as raw ELF bytes and
    the kernel parses them.

  - run_qemu points at the HDD path (renamed from run_qemu_hda);
    run_qemu_floppy is the old floppy path.

  - init_src/Makefile (+6 / -4), init_src/init.c (+5 / -4),
    kernel/process.c (1 l.), kernel/include/process.h (+3),
    kernel/include/common_defs.h (+9) -- matching plumbing.

Context (PR body):

  First time Tilck can run user programs that weren't compiled with
  the kernel. init becomes a real ELF file loaded at its requested
  virtual addresses, not a raw-binary dropped at a hard-coded offset.
  Sets up the rest of 2017's usermode work.

## 578efe6b -- Making init to be compiled with diet libc (#21)

Commit: 578efe6bd1...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Jan 10 22:03:10 2017 +0200

Message:

  This change finally makes init to be almost "normally" compiled.
  Now it is a regular ELF32 file, statically linked in died libc.
  Syscalls (only int 0x80 for now) work and also argc, argv and
  environ is passed to the program as well. This way, the testing
  can be much more "realistic".

  [plus a 17-bullet commit-by-commit log, ending in: adding diet
  libc to the toolchain / passing argc/argv via stack / adding
  env support.]

AI notes:

What changed:

  First user-space program compiled against a real libc.

  - build_toolchain.sh (+44 / -6) -- adds dietlibc to the toolchain
    (cloned into toolchain/dietlibc, built without
    -fstack-protector). The commit body notes dietlibc "seems to
    accept set_thread_area() to fail" -- important because Tilck
    doesn't implement TLS yet.

  - init_src -- complete cleanup: string.c (-188), string.h (-38),
    syscall_interface.h (-68), usermode_syscall_wrappers.h (-63),
    asmInit.asm (-9) all deleted. init.c (+12 / -16) now just calls
    libc functions.

  - init_src/Makefile (+27 / -6) -- links against libmusl / dietlibc
    with -nostdinc and -static.

  - New build_scripts/musl-gcc (6 l.) -- wrapper around gcc that sets
    the right -I/-L/-B for the musl-install tree.

  - kernel/i386/idt.c (+51 / -32) -- handles nested interrupts:
    tracks interrupt depth so the scheduler knows whether it's safe
    to preempt. kernel/i386/irq.c (+16 / -51) and kernel/i386/
    kernelAsm.asm (+34 / -26) -- matching generic irq-handler
    cleanup.

  - kernel/i386/process32.c (+64) -- sets up argc / argv / envp on
    the user stack before handing control to the new process. The
    kernel now follows the SysV x86 ABI for stack layout:
    [argc][argv[0]...argv[argc-1]][NULL][envp...][NULL].

  - kernel/syscalls.c (+30 / -44) -- syscall table shrinks slightly;
    a few debug handlers removed now that real libc syscalls flow
    through.

  - kernel/include/arch/generic_x86/utils.h (+39 / -5) -- more inline
    helpers pulled into generic-x86 (were in common_defs.h).

Context (PR body is the 17-commit log):

  Milestone: init is now a statically-linked ELF32 built against
  dietlibc, loaded by the ELF loader from PR #20, runs with a real
  SysV x86 stack layout, and calls back through int 0x80 for
  syscalls. Prior versions used a hand-written asm shim and a few
  dozen wrapper functions. This is the point where "userspace" is
  actually Unix-like.

## bc7cb57e -- Making the kernel to be linked with gcc instead of directly with
   ld

Commit: bc7cb57ef4...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Jan 11 20:38:24 2017 +0200

Message:

  This allows int64ops to be finally removed and it is strongly
  recommanded anywhere.

  BONUS: all variables in BSS have been removed.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/Makefile (+12 / -6) -- kernel link step switches from
    ld --start-group ... --end-group to gcc -nostdlib -lgcc
    -Wl,--start-group ... -Wl,--end-group. Linking through gcc means
    the toolchain's libgcc is automatically found, which provides
    the 64-bit arithmetic helpers.

  - kernel/i386/int64ops.s (-842) -- DELETED. The hand-imported
    libgcc routines for 64-bit arithmetic are no longer needed.

  - kernel/i386/gdt.c (+3 / -3), kernel/i386/idt.c (+2 / -2),
    kernel/term.c (1 l.) -- "all variables in BSS have been
    removed": the few remaining globals at file scope that GCC
    would put in .bss get explicit = {0} initializers so they go
    to .data and survive the objcopy strip.

  - top-level Makefile (1 l.) -- minor adjustment.

Context (body explains the "why"):

  The int64ops.s import was a workaround; linking via gcc solves the
  same problem with one line change. Zero-bss keeps the kernel image
  a contiguous blob that the bootloader can dd into place without
  needing a runtime .bss zero-init.

## cf4f2a10 -- adding an ifdef in elf_loader.c

Commit: cf4f2a1088...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Jan 15 18:35:54 2017 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/elf_loader.c (+3 l.) -- gates some printk debug output
  behind an #ifdef DEBUG, so release builds don't spam syscall
  traces.

================================================================================
  ERA 4 -- CMake, CI, preemptive kernel  (Jan 2017 - May 2017)
================================================================================

  The project becomes a build-system-first OS. CMake replaces the
  hand-written Makefiles across the whole tree; Travis CI runs the
  unit tests on every push; gcov + lcov report coverage. The
  bootloader learns to switch into unreal mode to load a FAT-formatted
  RAM disk at +128 MiB, so init is no longer a raw blob but a regular
  file in a filesystem image. Kernel-side: kernel threads become
  first-class (kthread_create with arg), tasklets defer IRQ work to
  process context, kmutex is the first sync primitive, then kcond
  (condition variables). Each user thread gets its own kernel stack,
  enabling real kernel preemption; kernel_yield() and kernel_sleep()
  arrive. Scheduler now runs on state lists (runnable / sleeping /
  zombie) and uses a dedicated idle_task_kthread. README + LICENSE
  (BSD 2-Clause) get added; current_task is renamed to current to
  match Linux convention. By the end of this era the kernel has most
  of the primitives a Unix-like kernel needs to start running real
  programs.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## f3865a34 -- Enhancing the bootloader (#23)

Commit: f3865a343c...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 5 12:16:51 2017 +0200

Message:

  This change makes the bootloader to enter in unreal mode in order to
  load more than 500 KB from the drive and put that at high addresses
  (+128 MB) accessible by the kernel.
  The idea is substantially to load a mem disk, and later making the
  kernel to mount it.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - bootloader/boot.asm (+279 / -52) -- large extension. New path
    enters "unreal mode": switches to 32-bit protected mode briefly,
    sets DS/ES limits to 4 GiB, drops back to real mode. Real-mode
    code can then use 32-bit addressing modes to write to addresses
    above 1 MiB. Uses it to load a memory disk image from sector N
    onward into physical memory starting at +128 MiB.

  - New kernel/crc32.c (103 l.) -- CRC-32 table + crc32(crc, buf,
    len) function (verbatim copy of Gary S. Brown's public-domain
    CRC-32 -- credited in the header). Used in kmain() to validate
    the memdisk load.

  - New exos.bochs (46 l.) -- Bochs config file for debugging.

  - New create_vmdk.sh (2 l.) -- short helper to wrap exos.img in a
    VMDK for VirtualBox/VMware testing.

  - kernel/main.c (+40 / -12) -- mount_memdisk() maps the loaded
    image into kernel virtual space; test_memdisk() dumps the first
    bytes and CRCs the whole thing to verify the bootloader load
    matched what was on disk.

  - CMakeLists.txt (+2 / -2), kernel/include/utils.h (+1),
    kernel/include/arch_utils.h (+2), run_qemu (1 l.) -- plumbing.

Context (PR body):

  With the memdisk approach, the bootloader can drop an arbitrary
  blob (later: a FAT filesystem) into kernel memory, which the
  kernel can then mount. No more "init at a hard-coded sector
  offset" -- you put init inside a filesystem image.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## b4559951 -- Adding BIOS parameter pack to the MBR (#24)

Commit: b45599513a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 5 18:23:34 2017 +0200

Message:

  * simplifying as much as possible the 1st stage to make room for
    the MBR metadata
  * adding bios parameter pack to the bootloader and making this way
    everything to work on my DELL XPS 13 9360
  * some refactoring
  * minor fixes and enhancements

AI notes:

What changed:

  - bootloader/boot.asm (+274 / -238) -- stage1 (first 512 bytes)
    gets a BIOS Parameter Block (BPB) embedded at the expected
    offset. Some PC BIOSes (notably on the author's DELL XPS 13
    9360) refuse to boot an MBR that doesn't have the BPB at the
    right position, because they interpret the volume as FAT. The
    BPB satisfies their check; the rest of stage1 is trimmed to make
    room.

  - CMakeLists.txt (+2 / -2), kernel/arch/i386/idt.c (+2),
    kernel/main.c (+3) -- minor.

Context (subject + body):

  Real-hardware compatibility fix driven by a specific machine.
  First commit that mentions compatibility with a named consumer
  laptop.

## 58d6fa0a -- Using fat memdisk (#25)

Commit: 58d6fa0ae4...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 5 21:45:30 2017 +0200

Message:

  * adding a simple build fat script
  * making the kernel to load init from the ram disk

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New build_scripts/build_fatpart.sh (11 l.) -- dd's a 16 MiB
    zero-filled image, mformat's a FAT filesystem on it
    (-T 32768 -h 16 -s 64), mcopies the init binary into the root.

  - kernel/main.c (+13 / -26) -- run_usermode_init() now reads init
    from RAM_DISK_VADDR + INIT_PROGRAM_MEM_DISK_OFFSET (0x23e00) --
    the offset where init ends up inside the FAT image. The
    temporary-map-the-elf-file-into-kernel-space-and-then-unmap
    dance is gone; the ELF sits in the already-mapped ramdisk.

  - kernel/elf_loader.c (+4 / -4), kernel/include/arch_utils.h
    (+3 / -2), bootloader/boot.asm (+3), debug_run_qemu (1 l.),
    CMakeLists.txt (+6 / -2) -- plumbing.

Context (subject):

  Init is no longer a raw blob at a fixed sector -- it's a regular
  file in a FAT filesystem that the bootloader loads as a memdisk.
  Foundation for a real VFS + multiple user programs later.
