## 938c54f9 -- [pageframe_allocator] Make kernel to set reserved MBs at
   runtime

Commit: 938c54f96d...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Feb 22 17:28:20 2018 +0200

Message:

  Since it is not very flexible to have the pageframe allocator
  to have at compile time the amounts of initial physical memory
  reserved, the func mark_pageframes_as_reserved() has been
  introduced. It is called in main() after the initialization
  of the pageframe allocator. This allows the ultimate
  flexibility, necessary in order to support for example any
  arbitrary physical address for the RAMDISK via multiboot
  [not implemented yet]. Implementing this change, required
  the introduction of a dedicated INVALID_PADDR == -1, since,
  at least in the unit tests, now 0 is a valid return value
  for the alloc functions.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New kernel/include/pageframe_allocator.h (56 l.) -- public
    API header for the allocator. Declares init_*, alloc_*,
    free_*, mark_pageframes_as_reserved. Previously these
    symbols scattered between paging.h and inline kernel code.

  - kernel/include/paging.h (-34) -- lots of exports move to
    the new dedicated header.

  - kernel/pageframe_allocator.c (+42 / -34) -- new
    mark_pageframes_as_reserved(paddr, size) reserves a
    physical region at runtime. init_pageframe_allocator no
    longer hardcodes "first 2 MB reserved"; that's now
    main.c's job after init.

  - INVALID_PADDR = -1 introduced as the failure sentinel so 0
    can be a legitimate return value in tests.

  - kernel/main.c (+3 / -3) -- calls mark_pageframes_as_reserved
    for the kernel-image region and the ramdisk region based on
    the actual RAMDISK_PADDR / RAMDISK_SIZE config.

  - kernel/paging_pageframe_allocator.c (+2 / -2),
    kernel/self_tests/perftests.c (+3 / -3),
    kernel/kmalloc_util.c (+2 / -2), kernel/elf_loader.c
    (+2 / -2), unittests/*.cpp (+45 / -22) -- matching.

Context (PR body explains the why):

  Compile-time reserved regions don't work when the ramdisk can
  live anywhere (multiboot-loaded kernel could get a memory
  map in any layout). Runtime reservation is the flexible
  alternative; this commit lays the groundwork.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 55fe7147 -- [kmalloc] Add a linear-mapping region in the kernel virtual
   space

Commit: 55fe7147db...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Feb 24 16:36:45 2018 +0200

Message:

  This change makes the first 256 MB of the physical memory to
  be linearly mapped at +KERNEL_BASE_VA (0xC0000000). This
  makes the allocator much faster (as the new perf tests prove),
  allows to switch between paddrs and vaddr by just using an
  offset and finally allows the removal of the 'paddr' field in
  page_directory_t.

AI notes:

What changed:

  Significant: Tilck adopts the Linux-style "direct map" of
  physical memory in the kernel's virtual address space.

  - kernel/main.c (+15 / -12), kernel/arch/i386/paging.c
    (+15 / -15) -- early paging init sets up a 256 MiB
    identity-style mapping at 0xC0000000 = phys 0x0, via 4 MiB
    PTEs (64 entries in the kernel page directory).

  - kernel/include/paging.h (+7 / -3) -- LINEAR_MAPPING_*
    macros: LINEAR_MAPPING_SIZE, PADDR_TO_VADDR(p) = p +
    KERNEL_BASE_VA, VADDR_TO_PADDR inverse. Constant-time
    pointer conversion for anything in that range.

  - common/include/config.h (+5), kernel/include/arch/i386/
    paging_int.h (-2) -- drops the page_directory_t.paddr
    field (redundant now that VADDR_TO_PADDR is a simple
    addition).

  - kernel/kmalloc_util.c (+16) -- kbasic_virtual_alloc/free
    can bypass map_page/unmap_page entirely for addresses
    inside the linear-mapping region. Huge speedup on the hot
    path.

  - kernel/elf_loader.c (+6 / -6), unittests/kmalloc_mocks.cpp
    (+4), .vscode/settings.json (+2 / -1) -- plumbing.

Context (PR body):

  Matches Linux's VMALLOC_START / PAGE_OFFSET split. For the
  common case (kmalloc that happens to pull from already-
  mapped physical memory) the allocator no longer needs to
  touch page tables at all; vaddr = paddr + KERNEL_BASE_VA.
  kmalloc perf jumps markedly on the new measurements.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 1487f842 -- [kmalloc] Remove logic handling allocation for metadata nodes

Commit: 1487f84269...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Feb 24 16:53:37 2018 +0200

Message:

  The allocation for metadata nodes logic was necessary to allow
  even the pages containing the metadata nodes (1 per block) to
  not be necessarily mapped. The function
  evenually_allocate_page_for_node() had the essencial role to
  allocate some pages for a given node and its neighbour nodes.
  In particular, since the size of one node is just 1 byte while
  the that function used to map 32KB at a time, that allowed the
  allocation for metadata nodes to be a rare thing.

  Now that linear mapping is used, keeping the logic for
  allocation of metadata nodes seems not really necessary.
  Kmalloc will support in the future different heaps, for sure
  also outside the linear mapping region, but, it seems
  inefficient to burn cycles for checking, for each node, if it
  has an actual mapping. It will be more convenient to just
  pre-map the whole area containing the metadata nodes when the
  heap is created.

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/kmalloc.c (-44), kernel/include/kmalloc.h (-11) --
  evenually_allocate_page_for_node, node_has_page, and the
  allocation_for_metadata_nodes bitmap all go away. Metadata
  pages are now assumed pre-mapped (caller's responsibility).
  Simplifies the hot path significantly.

Context (PR body is explicit):

  The lazy-metadata-page trick was a clever workaround for
  pre-linear-mapping days. With 256 MiB linearly mapped
  upfront, the whole metadata region is trivially accessible;
  the check per node was pure overhead. Expect another visible
  speedup in the perftest.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## d68a9c28 -- [kmalloc] Error checking in kzmalloc

Commit: d68a9c285d...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>

AI notes:

  kernel/include/kmalloc.h (+4) -- adds a kzmalloc(size)

  kmalloc return for NULL before the bzero. Previously callers
  had to do the null check themselves; kzmalloc consolidates.

## febf48bf -- [kmalloc] Make initialize_kmalloc() to create more heaps as
   fill the mem

Commit: febf48bfab...

What changed:

  - kernel/kmalloc.c (+61 / -13) --
    initialize_kmalloc() now walks the linear-mapping region
    carving out multiple heaps: each heap is a power-of-two
    chunk (e.g. 64 MiB, 32 MiB, 16 MiB, ...) filling the

    (1 l.) -- test scaffolding adjustment.

  many heaps as fit in linearly-mapped RAM, sized to minimize
  fragmentation.

## 5838f0d3 -- [paging] Use 4MB pages for the linear mapping

Commit: 5838f0d33a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Feb 27 12:59:03 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/arch/i386/paging.c (+36 / -50) -- switches the linear-
  mapping construction from 4 KiB PTEs (requiring 256 page
  tables for 1 GiB) to 4 MiB large pages (requiring only 256
  entries total in the page directory, no page tables). Uses
  the PDE.PS bit plus CR4.PSE. Saves ~1 MB of page-table
  memory and speeds up TLB walks.

Context (guess -- subject):

  Performance and simplicity win. 4 MiB pages are lightly-
  used compared to 4 KiB pages (which stay for user-mode
  processes), but perfect for a large contiguous identity
  mapping of the low physical region.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## d463daf1 -- [paging] Make the linear mapping to be 512 MB and add
   get_phys_mem_size()

Commit: d463daf1f2...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Feb 27 13:02:24 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - common/include/config.h (+3 / -3) -- LINEAR_MAPPING_MB
    bumped to 512 (was 256). The kernel virtual address
    space [0xC0000000, 0xE0000000) now covers 512 MiB of
    physical memory. With 4 MiB pages this costs only 128
    page-directory entries.

  - kernel/include/paging.h (+4 / -1), kernel/arch/i386/
    paging.c (+2 / -1) -- get_phys_mem_size() accessor (the
    actual detected RAM size, rounded down to power of two).
    Needed so the mapping loop knows when to stop if the
    machine has less than 512 MiB RAM.

## 40371ee1 -- Remove the paging_pageframe_allocator

Commit: 40371ee1a9...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Feb 27 13:07:19 2018 +0200

Message:

  After the introduction of the linear mapping for the whole
  kernel heap, instead as a special case for the first 4 MB
  and, after the introduction of the 4 MB pages for that
  linear mapping, the pageframe allocator for the paging
  become pointless (4 MB pages don't need page tables).

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/paging_pageframe_allocator.c deleted (-78).
  - unittests/paging_pageframe_allocator_test.cpp deleted
    (-66).
  - kernel/pageframe_allocator.c (-3) -- strips references.

Context (PR body):

  The paging-specific allocator was born in commit 4cc69082
  (2016-11) to guarantee that map_page() always had a
  physical page to use for a page table without competing
  with kmalloc. With 4 MiB pages for the linear mapping, the
  kernel no longer allocates 4 KiB page tables at all for
  its own address space -- the special pool becomes dead
  weight. End of an era for that allocator.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 65a3eaa5 -- [kmalloc] Fixing the failure of the chaos test

Commit: 65a3eaa5cd...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Feb 27 22:17:58 2018 +0200

Message:

  The problem was related with a bug in set_free_uplevels()
  which did not set the current node full = 0 in case one of
  the children was not full.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/kmalloc.c (+3) -- the actual fix: three lines in
    set_free_uplevels. When a kfree merge couldn't coalesce
    (one child still allocated), the parent's .full bit should
    still flip to 0 because *some* child now has free space.
    Previously it flipped only when BOTH children became
    free. The bug caused the parent to look "full" to
    subsequent allocs, hiding usable space.

  - unittests/kmalloc_test.cpp (+25 / -33) -- test code
    cleanup (the reproducer scaffolding is no longer needed).

  - kernel/include/kmalloc.h (1 l.), kernel/kmalloc_debug.h
    (+9 / -3) -- plumbing.

Context (body explains):

  3-line fix, 3-day hunt. Commit message is unusually precise
  about the root cause. Buddy-allocator parent-state
  maintenance is subtle.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## a10c57be -- [kmalloc] Improve SIMULATED_CALL()

Commit: a10c57be4e...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Feb 28 14:08:46 2018 +0200

Message:

  This changes makes internal_kmalloc() simpler by making
  SIMULATED_CALL() to automatically generate a label and
  store its address in alloc_stack. This way, in case the
  simulated call failed the control flow continues at the
  caller site as if the simulated call was a real one. No
  need anymore for a explicit and ugly labels like
  "after_left_call".

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/kmalloc.c (+32 / -33) -- uses GCC's && unary operator
  (computed goto / labels-as-values) to capture the return
  address in the iterative alloc_stack. The SIMULATED_CALL
  macro expands to a block that stores &&after_label and
  jumps to the callee; the callee's SIMULATED_RETURN does
  goto *alloc_stack[--sp].ret_addr. Removes 2 explicit
  after_left_call / after_right_call labels; the flow is
  now symmetric to a real call/return. kernel/CMakeLists.txt
  (+1) -- adds -Wno-gnu-label-as-value flag to permit the
  extension.

Context (PR body):

  Nicer code. Functionally identical to the explicit-label
  version, but reads like standard C control flow.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 86430b25 -- [multiboot] Start working on multiboot support

Commit: 86430b2538...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 1 11:48:16 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/arch/i386/entry.S (+17) -- prepends a Multiboot 1
  header (magic 0x1BADB002) at the start of the kernel's
  .text. When a Multiboot-compliant bootloader (GRUB, etc.)
  loads the kernel, it sees this header and can hand off
  control with a memory map etc. already set up.

Context (subject):

  First step toward GRUB compatibility. Tilck's own bootloader
  stays primary; Multiboot becomes an alternative entry point.

## 3f6e7619 -- [build] Make the kernel build to use a custom linker script

Commit: 3f6e761985...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 1 21:21:38 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - New kernel/arch/i386/linker_script.ld (53 l.) -- explicit
    kernel-side linker script. ENTRY(_start); places .text at
    KERNEL_LOAD_VADDR (0xC0100000); then .rodata, .data,
    .bss. Exposes __bss_start / __bss_end symbols for runtime
    clearing if ever needed.

  - kernel/arch/CMakeLists.txt (+10 / -1) -- LINK_FLAGS
    points at the new linker script.

Context (subject):

  Multiboot needs the kernel to start with a specific header
  at a known offset. An explicit linker script is the way to
  enforce that; ld -Ttext= wasn't precise enough.

Commit: 6117a20bef...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>

  headers, now qemu can correctly load the exOS kernel this
  way:

     qemu-system-i386 -m 256 -kernel ./build/elf_kernel_stripped

  Clearly, this is not enough since also the ramdisk has to be
  loaded too.

  PHDR gets an explicit AT(paddr) telling the ELF loader the

  up the paddr for its bootstrap.

  bootloader). For development iteration, saves the "rebuild
  image, flash, reboot" cycle.

## a06fa108 -- [entry] Make entry.S much simpler

Commit: a06fa1084c...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Mar 2 12:38:37 2018 +0200

Message:

  First, 4-MB pages are used: this way is much simpler to get
  the same result as before. No need to create a page table
  in addition to the page directory. Second, this simpler code
  can be written by avoiding to use the registers EAX and EBX
  which might contain multiboot info.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/arch/i386/entry.S (+45 / -61) -- big simplification.
    The early boot identity-map construction no longer builds
    a 4 KiB page table + page directory pair; it builds a
    page directory with 4 MiB entries directly (PSE). Halves
    the code. Also rearranges register use to preserve EAX /
    EBX (which Multiboot puts magic + MBI-pointer in) across
    the setup.

  - kernel/arch/i386/paging.c (1 l.) -- trivial.

Context (body):

  The 4-MiB-pages switch (commit 5838f0d3) for the main
  linear mapping makes it natural for early boot to also
  use 4 MiB pages. Simpler code, preserves the registers
  carrying Multiboot data.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Commit: e42b5fde8f...

  After adding the scripts (with and w/o KVM) to run QEMU with

  completely disappears.

  Out-of-tree builds (parallel debug and release dirs) made

Commit: d39aafb561...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 3 17:19:42 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  PHDRS { text PT_LOAD; rodata PT_LOAD; data PT_LOAD; }
  declaration at the top. Each section is then assigned to
  a specific PHDR with :text / :rodata / :data. Gives the

  up in the ELF; matches what a normal-executable linker
  script looks like.

AI notes:

What changed:

  New scripts/build_apps/make_symtabs_loadable.c (112 l.) --
  host-side C tool. Post-link, edits the kernel ELF to mark
  its .symtab / .strtab sections as SHF_ALLOC (loadable) so
  they get actually loaded into memory at boot (instead of
  being kept purely as debug info that objcopy strips). Then
  the in-kernel symbol lookup code has access to the real
  tables. First C utility program living under scripts/.

## 31e8bf15 -- [elfhack] Fix a bug drop_last_section causing the ELF to loose
   .shstrtab

Commit: 31e8bf15c6...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 6 21:47:15 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - scripts/build_apps/elfhack.c (+110 / -2) -- adds logic to
    preserve .shstrtab even when dropping the last section.
    The section-header-string-table is referenced by every
    section's sh_name index; dropping it broke most ELF
    tools. The new code rewrites the section header order so
    the dropped sections aren't actually the last one in the
    SHT (the previous assumption didn't hold when .shstrtab
    was last by linker convention).

  - kernel/arch/CMakeLists.txt (+2) -- adds an --assert-
    section-found=.shstrtab step to catch the bug class.

## 9a422228 -- Introducing find_addr_of_symbol()

Commit: 9a4222284d...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 12 18:27:08 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/elf_loader.c (-121 / +0) -- strips out all the
    in-elf_loader.c symbol-walking code (moved to
    debug_utils.c where it actually gets used).

  - kernel/debug_utils.c (+35 / -9) -- gains
    find_addr_of_symbol(name) + find_symbol_by_addr(addr).
    The former walks .symtab looking for a matching
    Elf32_Sym.st_name; the latter finds the nearest symbol
    with st_value <= addr < st_value + st_size.

  - kernel/include/debug_utils.h (+2 / -1) -- declarations.

  - kernel/main.c (+3 / -4) -- uses the new API at boot.

Context (subject + the refactor):

  Symbol lookup is a debug-utilities concern, not an ELF-
  loading concern. Now that the tables are loaded by
  elf_loader and stashed in misc.c, debug_utils owns the
  lookup primitive. Dump_stacktrace in debug_utils.c can
  directly call find_symbol_by_addr to print names.

## 5a0620d8 -- [asm] Introduce macros making asm functions marked as function
   symbols

Commit: 5a0620d86e...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 13 13:29:17 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - common/include/config.h (+8) -- FUNC(name) and
    END_FUNC(name) macros that expand to GAS directives:
    .type name, @function; name:; ... .size name, . - name.
    Ensures .symtab has proper STT_FUNC entries for asm
    symbols, with accurate sizes.

  - kernel/arch/i386/entry.S (+23 / -16), irq_handlers.S
    (+7 / -5), isr_handlers.S (+14 / -10) -- asm entry
    points wrapped in FUNC/END_FUNC. Required so
    find_symbol_by_addr can size-bound them correctly.

  - scripts/build_apps/elfhack.c (+1) -- tiny.

Context (subject):

  Before this, asm symbols were STT_NOTYPE with st_size = 0,
  which confused find_symbol_by_addr (any address would
  match the nearest asm label, no matter how far). Now the
  size check works.

## 821ca77d -- [paging] Fix is_mapped() to support 4-MB pages

Commit: 821ca77dce...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 13 13:55:23 2018 +0200

Message:

  This allows the stackwalk32() debug function to work.
  Now pretty symbolic backtraces seem to work everywhere in
  exOS.

  BONUS:
   - make debug_run_qemu to use multiboot_nokvm in order to
     allow the self tests to be run with just -append
     -s=<selftest name>

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/arch/i386/paging.c (+6) -- is_mapped now handles
    page_dir_entry.psize == 1 (4 MiB huge-page entries) by
    short-circuiting: if the PDE is present and PSIZE,
    every vaddr in that 4 MiB range is mapped. Previously
    it walked to the (non-existent) page table and returned
    false for linearly-mapped addresses.

  - kernel/debug_utils.c (+7 / -6) -- the stack walker can
    now validate frame pointers even inside the linear
    mapping, where is_mapped used to lie.

  - scripts/debug_run_qemu (1 l.) -- switches to multiboot_
    nokvm so the -append cmdline reaches the kernel.

Context (subject):

  Panic backtraces were silently truncating at the first
  frame inside the linear-mapped region (= every kernel-
  code frame). With this fix stackwalk walks all the way up.

## 9e98f825 -- [fat32] Remove a wrong ASSERT from the FAT32 code

Commit: 9e98f8255a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 13 20:10:29 2018 +0200

Message:

  The ASSERT(to_read == d->cluster_size) made sense only in
  the original fat_read_whole_file() function, which source
  has been used to write fat_read(). After the introduction
  of fseek(), clearly that ASSERT could not be kept in
  fat_read().

  BONUS: this change fixes another issue as well: the failure
  of the fseek unit test with a "buffers differ" error, in
  the case of read 0: in this case, the issue is simply the
  fact that the buffers (on stack) contain garbage since
  fseek returned 0. The fix is simply to zero the buffers
  before reading.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - common/fat32_base.c (-16 / +1) -- drops the
    cluster-alignment ASSERT inherited from read_whole_file.
    With fseek, partial-cluster reads are legitimate.

  - unittests/exvfs_test.cpp (+6 / -2) -- bzero the
    buffers before calling exvfs_read so the "bytes
    compared to nothing" case no longer sees random
    stack garbage.

## 0094d1be -- [paging] Remove the page_tables field from page_directory_t

Commit: 0094d1be19...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 15 14:20:27 2018 +0200

Message:

  Now that linear mapping is used, not only page_directory_t
  doesn't need a 'paddr' field, but also does not need to keep
  a separate array with the vaddrs of the page tables: they're
  addresses can be calculated from their physical address, by
  just adding an offset.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/include/arch/i386/paging_int.h (+1 / -2) -- removes
    page_tables[1024] from page_directory_t. The struct
    shrinks from ~12 KiB to 4 KiB.

  - kernel/arch/i386/paging.c (+25 / -34) -- call sites that
    used pdir->page_tables[i] now compute the vaddr via
    PADDR_TO_VADDR(pdir->entries[i].ptaddr << 12). No extra
    bookkeeping.

  - kernel/include/paging.h (1 l.) -- trivial.

Context (PR body):

  Another benefit of linear mapping: the "C-side pointer to
  page table" cache becomes redundant. Saves 4 KiB per
  process (= per pdir), plus eliminates a class of bugs where
  the two views could get out of sync.

## 864cb5e4 -- [paging] Rename 'pageTableAddr' to 'ptaddr'

Commit: 864cb5e41e...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 15 14:57:45 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/arch/i386/paging.c (+11 / -13),
  kernel/include/arch/i386/paging_int.h (+1 / -1) -- field
  rename pageTableAddr -> ptaddr inside page_dir_entry_t.
  Kills the last camelCase field in the paging structs.

Context (this commit is later referenced as tag z-ancient-09):

  Matches the final naming convention. As docs/
  ancient_commits.md notes, this commit is tagged z-ancient-09
  -- the first commit in the Ubuntu 18.04 era.

================================================================================
  ERA 6 -- Interactive user mode  (Mar 2018 - ...)
================================================================================

  With the kernel's filesystem, ELF loader, symbols, backtraces, and
  preemption now all working reliably, this era is about making Tilck
  actually useable from a user-mode program. In about one intense week
  it lands: real open/close/read/write/ioctl syscalls backed by a VFS
  dispatch; devfs with /dev/tty0; a char-device driver framework
  (kernel/char/) and the first driver (tty); cooked-mode keyboard input
  so userland read(0, ...) blocks until Enter and returns a line; a
  proper kcond-based waitpid replacing the demo implementation; a
  working sys_execve that destroys the caller's pdir and loads a new
  ELF in place; the usermode_apps/ directory replacing usermode_init/
  as a place for multiple user programs; /bin/shell as the first
  real interactive program (cd / exit / help builtins, fork+exec for
  external commands). term splits into a generic "terminal" on top of
  a video_interface abstraction so a framebuffer driver can slot in
  later. kmalloc gains a proper mutex and a calculate_block_size
  function enabling size-less kfree(). By the end of this era, booting
  Tilck drops into a shell prompt; you can type "cd /bin", "help",
  "shell" (nested shells), read files, etc.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## ce3234b8 -- [FS] Make userland to write() to console through devfs

Commit: ce3234b814...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 14 16:29:29 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  First real devfs. Userland write(fd=1, ...) now reaches
  the kernel console through the file-ops dispatch
  infrastructure, not a hardcoded path in sys_write.

  - New kernel/fs/devfs.c (79 l.) -- devfs_mount_at(path)
    registers a filesystem that exposes pseudo-files.
    Creates /dev/tty0 whose file_ops.write calls term_
    write_char().

  - New kernel/include/fs/devfs.h (6 l.) -- public API.

  - kernel/main.c (+8) -- mounts devfs at /dev at boot.

  - kernel/process.c (+10) -- on task-create, opens
    /dev/tty0 into fd 0, 1, 2 so stdin / stdout / stderr
    point at the console by default.

  - kernel/fs/fs_syscalls.c (+21) -- sys_write dispatches
    through fops.

  - usermode_init/init.c (+9) -- no longer needs special
    syscall wrappers for writing to the screen; regular
    write(1, ...) works.

  - kernel/arch/i386/process32.c (1 l.),
    kernel/syscalls.c (-16) -- plumbing.

Context (subject):

  Linux's "everything is a file" abstraction starts working
  for real in Tilck. A userland program writing to stdout
  goes: write(1, ...) -> int 0x80 -> sys_write ->
  fds[1].fops.write -> devfs_tty0_write -> term_write_char.

## a1dfbc2e -- [FS] Fix problems caused by use of stdio funcs in init

Commit: a1dfbc2e57...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 14 19:30:10 2018 +0200

Message:

  When stdio funcs are used, dietlibc's printf() doesn't just
  do a write(), but it checks with ioctl() if the current
  output is a tty. Since exOS didn't have ioctl() yet, the
  check failed and printf() assumed that there is no need to
  write line-by-line the output. Manually forcing the flush
  with fflush(stdout) works, but it should work also without
  it, as it does on Linux. Therefore, a specially crafted
  impl of ioctl() has been added in order to trick dietlibc.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/fs/fs_syscalls.c (+68) -- first sys_ioctl stub.
    Returns success for the specific TIOCGWINSZ-like probe
    dietlibc uses to detect a tty, so printf decides to
    line-buffer. Generic ioctl(2) dispatch to fd.fops.ioctl
    added.

  - New kernel/include/fs/devfs.h functions (+12) for tty-
    specific ioctls.

  - usermode_init/init.c (+26 / -27), usermode_init/
    CMakeLists.txt (+3) -- init switches from manual
    write()s to real printf() and friends; verifies line
    buffering works.

  - kernel/fs/devfs.c (-12), kernel/main.c (+3 / -1),
    kernel/syscalls.c (+5 / -1) -- plumbing.

Context (body is explicit):

  Userland libc quirks becoming visible. Real libraries
  make assumptions about the kernel supporting things like
  ioctl; stubbing just the right calls enough to satisfy
  those assumptions is the work here.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 8acc67ea -- [FS] Introducing a simple interface for char device drivers

Commit: 8acc67eab7...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>

    Wraps term_write_char() for output; sets up to host
    keyboard input eventually. Registers itself with devfs
    as "tty0" via the new API below.

    accepts per-device registration: each char driver
    provides its own read/write/ioctl callbacks, devfs
    routes by filename.

    subdirectory.

Context (subject):

  Kernel stops treating /dev/tty0 as a one-off. Any future
  char device (/dev/kb, /dev/null, /dev/zero, /dev/random)
  can now register itself the same way.

## d3b9a6e2 -- [KB] Make the keyboard cooked buffer a ring buffer

Commit: d3b9a6e2ee...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 17 11:22:33 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/arch/generic_x86/kb.c (+39 / -6) -- replaces the
    linear cooked buffer with a fixed-size ring buffer
    (power-of-two size via modulo-by-mask). Keyboard input
    arriving while a userland task holds the read lock no
    longer drops chars once the buffer fills -- it wraps,
    with old chars displaced.

  - kernel/char/tty.c (+5 / -16) -- reader side simpler now
    that the buffer is a ring.

  - kernel/include/kb.h (+8) -- exposes ring-buffer sanity
    checks.

  - kernel/tasklet.c (+3 / -3) -- trivial.

## 75e23911 -- [term] Move the term_buffer in BSS

Commit: 75e239111d...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 17 11:40:31 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/arch/generic_x86/term.c (+16 / -12) -- the scrollback
  buffer (1024 rows * 80 chars * 2 bytes = ~160 KiB) moves
  from a kmalloc'd allocation to a static file-scope array
  in .bss. Guarantees it's available before kmalloc is up,
  and the linear-mapping-aware kernel loader zero-fills it
  at load time regardless.

## 2134bb59 -- [term] Fix issue with invisible cursor

Commit: 2134bb595a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 17 19:46:43 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/arch/generic_x86/textmode_video.c (+12 / -8) --
  textmode_video was writing the cursor position to VGA
  ports (0x3D4/0x3D5) but forgot to re-enable the hardware
  cursor via the same ports (cursor start/end register
  0x0A/0x0B). After boot, no blinking cursor was visible.
  Fix explicitly resets start/end so the cursor shows.

## 75e51d14 -- [kb] Fix logic appending chars to the ring buffer

Commit: 75e51d14e9...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 17 20:18:43 2018 +0200

Message:

  Briefly, doing everything in a tasklet causes a small but
  noticeable delay at least in qemu when not run with -curses.
  This fix makes the writer (kb driver) to write in the ring
  buffer while the interrupts are disabled.

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/arch/generic_x86/kb.c (+18 / -13) -- the cooked-
  mode ring-buffer append moves from a tasklet (ran in
  process context after the IRQ) back into the IRQ handler
  itself, bracketed by disable_interrupts / enable_
  interrupts. Trades some IRQ-handler runtime for input
  responsiveness.

Context (body):

  Deferring to tasklet was the "right" layering; but the
  delay was user-perceptible. Pragmatic fix: keep the ring-
  buffer append fast-path in the IRQ. Complex processing
  (echo, line editing) still goes to the tasklet.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## ba2cb84e -- [term] Make term to use video_interface instead of hard-coded
   func calls

Commit: ba2cb84e6a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 18 12:38:22 2018 +0200

Message:

  With this change, the term code becomes generic and does not
  depend on how actually the characters are displayed on-screen.
  For the moment, still the only supported mode is the standard
  PC text mode (80x25), but this generalization will allows
  easily term to work with any other mode implementing the
  video_interface. For example, exOS may support a running its
  console in a graphical mode, with a framebuffer info passed
  by the bootloader. In that case, after implementing the
  video_interface functions to work with framebuffer, term
  will use them seamlessly.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/include/term.h (+23 / -0) -- declares
    struct video_interface containing function pointers:
    set_char_at(row, col, val), move_cursor(row, col),
    scroll_up(rows), etc.

  - kernel/arch/generic_x86/textmode_video.c (+20 / -22) --
    exposes a static textmode_video_if object populating
    video_interface with its functions.

  - kernel/arch/generic_x86/term.c (+33 / -27) -- term now
    takes a video_interface *vi at init time and calls
    vi->set_char_at etc. instead of textmode_video_plot
    directly.

  - kernel/main.c (+20 / -7) -- passes the text-mode video
    interface to term_init on boot; in the future, a fb
    video interface could be substituted.

  - kernel/include/arch/generic_x86/textmode_video.h
    (+11 / -9), bootloader/stage3.c (+6 / -3) -- plumbing.

Context (PR body is explicit):

  Generalization for framebuffer support. Once a
  framebuffer video driver lands, swap the video_interface
  and term doesn't know or care.

## e613a200 -- [kcond] Add support for timeout_ticks in kcond_wait()

Commit: e613a200bf...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 18 16:53:52 2018 +0200

Message:

  This super-useful feature allows kcond_wait() to timeout
  after some time, if its caller wants that. This feature is
  particularly useful for an use-case like the tasklet runner
  kthread: since it's signalled without any lock, it can
  happen that it may loose a signal, while running a tasklet.
  Thanks to the timeout_ticks, loosing a signal won't be a
  big deal.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/kcond.c (+21 / -9) -- kcond_wait gains a
    timeout_ticks parameter; if non-zero, registers a
    timer alongside the kcond wait so the task wakes up
    after the timeout even without a signal. Returns
    whether it was a signal or a timeout.

  - kernel/include/sync.h (+3 / -2) -- API change.

  - kernel/timer_handler.c (+25 / -20) -- the per-task
    timer list gains entries for kcond timeouts.

  - kernel/tasklet.c (1 l.) -- tasklet runner uses a non-
    zero timeout so missed signals don't stall it.

  - kernel/self_tests/testrunners.c (+29 / -5) -- new
    selftest for kcond_wait with timeout.

  - kernel/char/tty.c (1 l.), kernel/include/process.h
    (+5 / -2) -- matching.

Context (PR body):

  Lost-wakeup protection without needing the full "associated
  mutex" Linux discipline. Pragmatic: a missed signal is
  recovered at most one timeout later.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## e88613b0 -- [tasklet] Make the runner thread to run as many tasklets as
   possible

Commit: e88613b06d...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 18 16:59:47 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/tasklet.c (+7 / -1) -- tasklet-runner kthread, after
  waking from kcond_wait, drains the queue in a loop until
  empty instead of running just one tasklet then waiting
  again. Reduces wake-up overhead when a burst of tasklets
  arrives.

## e9427294 -- [process] Implement (partially) waitpid() properly

Commit: e942729430...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 18 20:26:37 2018 +0200

Message:

  The previous impl. of waitpid() was just a mini-demo to
  test that a user task can be preempted while running in
  kernel and that the resume after that will work correctly.
  Now that we're sure that works, it didn't make any more
  sense to keep that impl. Therefore, a proper notification
  mechanism has been used to achieve that.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/process.c (+52 / -24) -- sys_waitpid(pid) now uses
    a per-parent kcond: parent calls kcond_wait on its own
    wait_chld condition; child's exit path
    (task_change_state TASK_STATE_ZOMBIE + kfree parent
    notification) signals it. Handles pid == -1 (any child),
    specific pid, and ECHILD when no children.

  - kernel/include/process.h (+1 / -1),
    kernel/include/sync.h (+2 / -1) -- declarations.

  - kernel/arch/i386/paging.c (+5 / -5) -- small adjustments.

  - common/include/common_defs.h (1 l.) -- tiny.

  - usermode_init/init.c (+8 / -5) -- now forks a child,
    waits for it, asserts the child's exit status.

Context (PR body):

  waitpid was a debug demo from the kernel-preemption era.
  Real kcond-based implementation now works end-to-end.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 6779b15b -- [process] Add parent_pid to task_info

Commit: 6779b15b88...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 18 20:33:20 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/include/process.h (+4 / -3) -- adds int parent_pid
    to task_info. Set at fork() to current->pid.

  - kernel/process.c (+2 / -1), kernel/sched.c (1 l.) --
    propagate it; sys_waitpid filters children by
    parent_pid == current->pid.

Context (subject):

  waitpid needs to know its children; the list_node was
  there but no back-pointer. Simpler to keep a parent_pid
  field than walk the whole task list.

## aadf9fd4 -- [syscalls] Make unimplemented syscalls to return -1

Commit: aadf9fd4df...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 18 20:44:24 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/syscalls.c (+23 / -23) -- unimplemented syscall stubs
  switch from "return 0" (silent success) to "return -1"
  (-EPERM). Saves debugging time: libc code that depends on
  an unimplemented syscall now gets an explicit error
  instead of proceeding with garbage results.

## 980ba310 -- [build] Make scripts/cmake_run to work with any build directory

Commit: 980ba310ef...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 19 12:01:11 2018 +0200

Message:

  Until now, scripts/cmake_run was usable only in the project's
  main dir and it prepared the build to be in MAIN_DIR/build.
  Now, it's possible to create a build directory anywhere and
  just run MAIN_DIR/scripts/cmake_run there. The script will
  use that directory as a build directory and will also copy
  there all of the handy scripts for running qemu.

AI notes:

What changed:

  scripts/cmake_run (+14 / -6) -- if the script is invoked
  with $PWD != project root, use $PWD as the build directory
  instead of $PROJ_ROOT/build. Enables parallel build trees
  (debug/, release/, coverage/, etc.) without cd-ing back to
  the project root for each. The launchers (run_qemu etc.)
  are copied into whatever build dir gets used.

Context (body is explicit):

  Brings Tilck's build ergonomics closer to standard CMake
  workflows where people keep several build dirs per repo.
  Starts to feel like a normal open-source project to work on.

## 8b9497a0 -- [process] Fix a simple bug in execve()

Commit: 8b9497a02b...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 19 18:43:01 2018 +0200

Message:

  See the added comment.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/process.c (+9 / -1) -- the bug and its fix come
    with the added comment: after pdir_destroy on the old
    pdir, the task briefly has no valid address space
    while the loader maps the new one in. If an interrupt
    fires during that window, context_switch walks a dead
    pdir. Fix: disable_preemption bracket around the
    destroy/load sequence.

    (prints its PID; reads a line from stdin) to verify

## a81a21c4 -- [kmalloc] Add memory poisoning to catch use-after-free bugs

Commit: a81a21c49a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 20 15:21:18 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/kmalloc.c (+8) -- in debug builds, kfree() fills
    the freed block with 0xABABABAB before returning it to
    the free list. Subsequent reads from a dangling pointer
    see the obvious marker, subsequent writes corrupt the
    marker instead of a just-reallocated block (makes the
    bug visible).

  - kernel/process.c (+6 / -4) -- fixes a use-after-free
    that the poisoning immediately surfaced (likely in the
    fork + exec + exit interaction).

Context (guess -- subject):

  Debug aid. exOS's allocator is still shaking out sharp-
  pointer bugs as the process subsystem matures.

## 80d07d51 -- [fs] Add dup to filesystem and use it sys_fork()

Commit: 80d07d5198...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 20 17:06:01 2018 +0200

Message:

  The addition of a dup(fs_handle) function was essential in
  order to allow a parent to keep its file handles after a
  child dies (the kernel closes its file handles).

  NOTE: the memory poisoning by kfree() has been commented
  because it was making the kmalloc unit-tests to fail. The
  failure will be investigated.

What changed:

  - kernel/include/fs/exvfs.h (+3 / -1) -- file_ops gains
    a dup() callback.

  - kernel/fs/exvfs.c (+10) -- exvfs_dup calls fops->dup
    on a handle, returns a new handle referring to the same
    underlying file.

  - common/fat32_base.c (+11 / -1), kernel/fs/devfs.c
    (+12 / -2) -- dup implementations for FAT and devfs.

  - kernel/process.c (+9 / -3) -- sys_fork now duplicates
    the parent's open handles into the child; child kfree
    / exit no longer invalidates the parent's.

  - usermode_apps/shell.c (+7 / -5) -- matching.

  - kernel/kmalloc.c -- poisoning commented out per the
    note (the unit tests hadn't accounted for the marker).

regression).

## b6e173e2 -- [kmalloc] Introduce kmalloc_mutex

Commit: b6e173e2c5...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 20 21:15:47 2018 +0200

Message:

  This allows kmalloc() and kfree() to be used without
  disabling the preemption and it is, clearly, the proper
  solution.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - kernel/kmalloc.c (+17 / -5) -- introduces kmalloc_mutex
    (a kmutex); kmalloc / kfree lock it for the duration of
    their heap mutation. Callers no longer need to wrap in
    disable_preemption.

Context (body):

  Proper concurrency primitive. disable_preemption was the
  old blunt-hammer approach; a mutex is the right granular
  approach, especially once kernel threads start using
  kmalloc concurrently.

## cb8997c1 -- [process] Reduce the size of the non-preemptable code in
   execve()

Commit: cb8997c1bc...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 20 21:28:02 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/process.c (+29 / -19) -- narrows the
  disable_preemption window inside sys_execve to exactly the
  "swap the pdir + update task_info.pdir" step. Everything
  else (pdir_destroy, elf_loader) happens with preemption
  on. Better responsiveness: execve of a large binary no
  longer stalls the system.

  kernel/main.c (-1) -- trivial.

## 04e9e55d -- [kmalloc] Implement a working function to calculate block's
   size

Commit: 04e9e55d0e...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 21 00:58:57 2018 +0200

Message:

  The function calculate_block_size() is able to correctly
  calculate the size of any allocated block with kmalloc().
  It can be used by kfree() to remove the inconvenience of
  having a 2nd "size" paramater. The only drawback is that
  it has an overhead of about 25% in the worst case.

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/kmalloc.c (+12 / -20) -- finishes calculate_block_
  size: starts at the smallest block containing the
  pointer, walks upward looking for the "this node is the
  allocated boundary" marker in the buddy tree. Returns the
  size class of the original allocation.

Context (body is explicit):

  Prep for a nice-to-have API: kfree(ptr) without the size
  argument, matching standard libc. The 25% overhead stays
  as a known trade-off (most callers still pass size).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## bfc4e5e0 -- [kmalloc] Re-writing kfree() to not depend on 'size'

Commit: bfc4e5e0b5...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 21 01:25:49 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/kmalloc.c (+40 / -18) -- kfree(ptr) branches: if the
  caller passed size == 0, it calls calculate_block_size
  first. Otherwise the size-aware fast path runs. Previously
  size was mandatory.

## 019dcb15 -- [elf_loader] Fix a nasty bug: kfree() called with the WRONG
   size

Commit: 019dcb15b4...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 21 04:05:30 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/elf_loader.c (+7 / -5) -- the loader was calling
  kfree(buf, size) where size was the ELF segment's memsz
  (bytes) but the allocation had actually used pages_count
  (pages) * PAGE_SIZE -- slightly different rounding.
  Previously the allocator silently accepted the wrong
  size because it walked up to the right block anyway;
  calculate_block_size from the previous commit caught the
  discrepancy by disagreeing with the argument.

Context (subject):

  The size-less kfree infrastructure caught a real pre-
  existing bug in its first use. "Nasty" because the symptom
  was eventually a corrupted buddy tree.

## f2d78845 -- [kmalloc] Rename kfree() to kfree2()

Commit: f2d78845f8...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 21 04:35:52 2018 +0200

Message:

  Now kfree can work both with and without a size argument.
  The paramater can be completely removed, but it also makes
  some sense to have two versions of kfree: with and without
  the parameter size. The call-sites that know at compile-
  time the size of block that want to free can easily use
  kfree2 and a slightly faster kfree. The other sites, will
  just call the 1-parameter kfree() wrapper. In the next
  changes, this wrapper will be introduced.

AI notes:

What changed:

  Bulk rename across ~16 files: every existing kfree(ptr,
  size) call site is renamed to kfree2(ptr, size). Frees
  up the name kfree for the upcoming 1-arg wrapper.
  Touches bootloader/stage3.c, common/fat32_base.c,
  common/string_util.c, kernel/arch/i386/paging.c,
  kernel/elf_loader.c, kernel/fs/devfs.c, kernel/fs/exvfs.c,
  kernel/include/kmalloc.h, kernel/kmalloc.c, kernel/pq.c,
  kernel/process.c, kernel/sched.c,
  kernel/self_tests/perftests.c, unittests/CMakeLists.txt,
  unittests/kmalloc_mocks.cpp, unittests/kmalloc_test.cpp.

## 0ab7bd0d -- [kmalloc] Add a better debug-only fail-check for
   calculate_block_size

Commit: 0ab7bd0dea...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 21 15:13:42 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  kernel/kmalloc.c (+7 / -1) -- in debug builds, after
  calculate_block_size returns, double-checks the result
  by walking the buddy tree in the opposite direction
  (node-up from the claimed size). If the two disagree,
  panics with a descriptive message. Catches allocator-
  metadata corruption the poisoning alone can't detect.

## daa11cab -- [kmalloc] Fix minor bug detected by the kfree-mem-poisoning

## 3bb507c9 -- [entry] Move kernel's initial stack in BSS

Commit: 3bb507c9e4...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 21 17:25:28 2018 +0200

AI notes:

    stack (used before the scheduler switches to per-task
    stacks) moves from a hardcoded physical address to a
    BSS-reserved buffer via .space directive. Same reason as
    page_size_buf in commit 4c580338 -- stops colliding
    with low-memory BIOS data on real hardware.

  - common/include/config.h (-1) -- drops the hardcoded
    stack constant.

## de6a621d -- [fat32] Fix a triple fault in RELEASE builds with a NO_INLINE

Commit: de6a621df1...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 21 19:20:08 2018 +0200

Message:

  In RELEASE builds, reverse_long_name() [FAT32] gets inlined
  in fat_walk_directory in an apparently buggy way and that
  triggers a triple-fault. By just adding NO_INLINE everything
  works. It seems very likely a compiler bug.

AI notes:

What changed:

  - common/fat32_base.c (+6 / -1) -- reverse_long_name gets
    NO_INLINE attribute.

  - common/include/common_defs.h (+2 / -1) -- defines
    NO_INLINE as __attribute__((noinline)).

Context (body):

  Rare but real: toolchain bug forcing a workaround.
  Likely a miscompile around the stack array that
  reverse_long_name manipulates. Comment in code captures
  the context.

## 850adf67 -- [utils32] Run CLD at the end of memmove() [reverse_long_name()
   final FIX]

Commit: 850adf67c3...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladi32@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 22 20:58:00 2018 +0200

Message:

  The compiler has the right to assume that the DF flag is
  cleared. Unfortunately, exOS's memmove() did not clear it
  after using STD and that, caused the triple fault in
  reverse_long_name().

  For safety, a CLD has been added in boot.S and in entry.S.

AI notes:

What changed:

  The real root cause of the FAT triple-fault (commits
  de6a621d / d5b77feb investigated this).

  - kernel/arch/i386/utils32.c (+1) -- memmove, after using
    std + rep movsb for the backward-copy case, now ends
    with cld to restore the "string ops go forward" default.

  - bootloader/boot.S (+4), kernel/arch/i386/entry.S (+3)
    -- add explicit cld at early-boot entry as a belt-and-
    suspenders measure.

  - common/fat32_base.c (-13) -- removes the NO_INLINE
    workaround from commit de6a621d (no longer needed once
    the real bug is fixed).

Context (body is explicit):

  x86 ABI detail: DF must be 0 on function entry (compiler-
  generated memcpy/memmove rely on this). Tilck's memmove
  was leaving DF=1 in the STD path. Reverse_long_name
  happened to manifest it via struct-copy codegen that
  memcpy'd into a stack buffer; wrong direction = stack
  corruption.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 8d27dc05 -- Re-organize headers in the project [step 4]

Commit: 8d27dc052e...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Mar 23 15:55:25 2018 +0200

> Create kernel/ext_string_util.c and move there the functions using
> kmalloc in order to allow common/string_util.c to not depend on it.

AI notes:

What changed:

  52 lines removed from common/string_util.c, moved verbatim (+53) to
  the new kernel/ext_string_util.c. The extracted functions are the
  ones that call kmalloc() -- string duplicators / builders that
  allocate their result.

Context (from body):

  common/string_util.c is shared between kernel and bootloader; the
  bootloader has no kmalloc. Splitting out the allocating helpers into
  a kernel-only .c file lets common/ stay allocation-free and
  link-safely into the bootloader. Part of the recurring theme of
  making common/ truly "common".

## 133dcb0b -- Re-organize headers in the project [step 6]

Commit: 133dcb0b09...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Mar 23 16:13:13 2018 +0200

> Make common/string_util.c to NOT include any kernel code, not even
> under ifdef, by creating a printk() with WEAK linkage. In the
> kernel, the function has been re-implemented in kernel/printk.c.

AI notes:

What changed:

  +19 / -32 across 4 files. common/string_util.c loses ~20 lines of
  #ifdef-guarded kernel paths. bootloader/utils.c loses 13 lines (the
  bootloader's own printk stub, no longer needed now that a weak
  default exists). New kernel/printk.c (16 lines) provides the strong
  definition the kernel links against.
  include/common/common_defs.h gains the WEAK attribute declaration
  for printk().

Context (from body):

  The final step of the "common/ has no kernel deps" refactor.
  Previously common/string_util.c used #ifdef KERNEL to route
  diagnostics through the kernel printk -- clean in spirit but still
  pulled in kernel headers. Switching to a weak symbol inverts the
  dependency: the common code unconditionally calls printk(); whoever
  links (bootloader or kernel) provides the strong definition, or
  falls back to the no-op weak stub.

## ec82d6ab -- [tasklet] Intr. kcond_signal_single() and make the runner
   use it

Commit: ec82d6ab15...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Mar 23 18:10:38 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  +26 / -14 across 3 files. New kernel/kcond.c function
  kcond_signal_single(c, ti) that wakes exactly one named sleeping
  task waiting on condvar c (cancels timer, resets wait_obj, flips
  state to RUNNABLE). kcond_signal_int() is refactored to iterate and
  call kcond_signal_single() per matching task. kernel/tasklet.c now
  caches the tasklet runner task pointer at initialize_tasklets() and
  calls kcond_signal_single(&tasklet_cond, tasklet_runner_task)
  instead of the broadcast kcond_signal_all() on enqueue.

Context (guess -- no body):

  Optimisation: only one thread ever waits on tasklet_cond (the
  runner), so broadcasting is wasteful. Adding a targeted
  signal_single primitive lets the tasklet path avoid the O(n) walk
  of all sleeping tasks. Also a general-purpose addition -- other
  kernel code that knows *which* task it wants to wake can now do so
  directly.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 84fdc5f3 -- [tasklet] Quick fix for the broken unit tests

Commit: 84fdc5f34c...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Mar 23 18:23:02 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  +4 lines in kernel/tasklet.c. Likely defining tasklet_runner_task
  = NULL in the mock/test path or guarding the signal_single call so
  unit tests that don't spawn a real runner thread don't NULL-deref.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  The previous commit cached a task pointer produced by
  kthread_create() inside initialize_tasklets(). In the gtest build
  kthread_create may not run / returns NULL, breaking the new
  signal_single path. This is a tactical patch to unbreak CI, not a
  principled mock redesign.

## 8058afcf -- [string_util] Fix a bug in asm memcpy

Commit: 8058afcf7a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 24 18:41:04 2018 +0200

AI notes:

What changed:

  3 lines replaced in asm_x86_strings.h. The inline-asm memcpy held
  (n >> 2) in an input constraint tied to the "q" class and later
  reloaded it with `mov %0, %%ecx`, but the output constraint
  `"=q"(unused)` meant GCC was free to pick any byte-addressable
  register for the placeholder -- including one clobbered by the
  preceding `rep movsb`. Fix: pin the value to %ebx via `"b"(n>>2)`
  and reload explicitly with `mov %%ebx, %%ecx`.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Classic inline-asm constraint bug. Probably surfaced as intermittent
  data corruption in whatever test exercised non-4-byte-aligned
  copies. Writing correct x86 inline asm is notoriously finicky --
  this is the first of several micro-fixes to the new helpers.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 8c219bdc -- [asm_x86_strings] Emit non-inlined copies just once

Commit: 8c219bdc60...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 25 11:53:29 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +29 / -11 across 3 files. asm_x86_strings.h gets +31/-4: the
  inline-asm functions are likely split into a "static inline"
  declaration plus a "extern inline" / weak out-of-line definition,
  or switched to always-inline with a single real symbol emitted in
  one TU. common/string_util.c gains 2 lines -- the chosen TU that
  emits the out-of-line bodies. string_util.h loses 7 lines
  (redundant prototypes/macros).

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Problem: "inline" functions in headers, when not actually inlined
  by GCC (e.g. when taking their address, or in debug builds), get
  emitted in every translation unit -> linker multiple-definition
  errors, or one copy per TU and bloat. Standard C idiom: keep
  `static inline` + one non-inline definition in a single .c. Here
  common/string_util.c is designated as that "home" TU.

## 45cd69ff -- Use memcpy() instead of memmove() when possible

Commit: 45cd69ff13...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 25 12:34:51 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +25 / -22 across 10 files, mostly call sites. Every kernel caller
  where the src/dest ranges are known non-overlapping switches from
  memmove() to memcpy(): textmode_video.c (scroll buffer),
  arch/i386/paging.c, process32.c, char/tty.c, ext_string_util.c,
  fs/devfs.c, fs/fat32.c, process.c, tasklet.c. One line in
  asm_x86_strings.h -- probably changing memmove's internal
  helper call.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  memmove is correct always but has an overlap check + direction
  choice; memcpy is a straight forward rep movsd. Auditing call
  sites and using the cheaper primitive where legal is free
  performance. Would also reduce code size slightly since the
  inline memcpy is smaller than inline memmove.

## 7f57db00 -- [sched] Remove a buggy optimization in schedule()

Commit: 7f57db009b...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 25 19:27:02 2018 +0300

> The idea of just returning if selected == current worked great as
> well as schedule() was called by the timer interrupt handler, but
> it lead to weird issues in case schedule has been called
> indirectly by kernel_yield().

AI notes:

What changed:

  -10 lines total across entry.S, process32.c, and sched.c. The
  "if (selected == current) return;" fast-path is ripped out of
  schedule() and the associated fast-exit in entry.S is dropped.

Context (from body):

  The fast-path was safe only in the timer-interrupt context, where
  the caller has a well-defined iret frame ready. kernel_yield()
  drives schedule() from a synthetic context; returning early there
  left the yield state half-reverted, causing symptoms described
  vaguely as "weird issues". Correctness now first, will restore
  the optimisation in the next commit.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 5defb3f7 -- [FS] Optimize fat32_is_valid_filename_character() with
   a lookup array

Commit: 5defb3f7b4...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>

  a 256-entry bool/bit lookup table. The bulk of the new lines is
  the initialiser array itself, one flag per byte value.

## 86912a24 -- [process] Fix a race in sys_execve()

Commit: 86912a248b...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 26 18:24:30 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +17 / -22 in kernel/process.c. Flattens the nested
  disable_preemption / enable_preemption block around
  load_elf_program + task switch. Preemption is now disabled for
  the whole critical section; only on the "current == NULL"
  bootstrap path does it re-enable. The post-switch branch is
  simplified: if current was non-NULL the code never "re-disables"
  preemption -- switch_to_task inherits the already-disabled
  state.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Previously the code enabled preemption between the page-dir
  teardown and the switch_to_task call, opening a window where
  the task could be scheduled out mid-execve with a half-built
  address space. The fix keeps preemption disabled across the
  whole swap.

## 3cf11151 -- [kmalloc] Replace the kmalloc_mutex with disable/enable
   preemption

Commit: 3cf1115126...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 26 18:30:53 2018 +0300

> If even, theoretically, it is better for the allocator to have
> its own lock, that complicates the things since it does not allow
> (safely) non-preemptable code to call kmalloc/kfree. What could
> happen in that case is that the non-preemptable code might not be
> able to grab the kmalloc lock because other preemptable code
> holds it. This will end up in an ASSERT since the kmutex code
> won't be able to put succeed in calling kernel_yield. For a
> simple project like exOS, it is acceptable such a commonly used
> thing like the allocator to be called inside non-preemptable
> code. Also, considering that a kmalloc/kfree pair costs about
> 500-600 cycles that sounds not a big deal.

AI notes:

What changed:

  +5 / -7 in kernel/kmalloc.c. The kmalloc_mutex acquire/release
  bracketing the allocator's critical section is replaced by
  disable_preemption() / enable_preemption().

Context (from body):

  kmutex's wait path calls kernel_yield(), which is illegal in
  non-preemptable context -- so any kmalloc from an interrupt /
  tasklet / preemption-disabled path would ASSERT. Disabling
  preemption around the allocator's short critical section
  sidesteps that entirely at the (small, 500-600 cycle) cost of a
  full-kernel-wide non-preemptable window. Accepted tradeoff for a
  uniprocessor hobby kernel.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## fc053ea9 -- [elf_loader] Fix a bug in the calculation of page_count

Commit: fc053ea99d...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 26 19:14:20 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +17 / -11 in kernel/elf.c. The page_count computation for an ELF
  loadable segment is corrected. Likely problem: ceiling division
  didn't account for segments whose vaddr is mid-page (start
  offset not page-aligned), undercounting pages by one when the
  memsz crossed a page boundary.

Context (guess -- no body):

  Symptoms of this bug would be page faults near the end of the
  last page of an ELF segment. Critical for running binaries whose
  segments happen to straddle pages, which is almost always.

  per-program-header loop inside load_elf_program() is hoisted
  into a new static helper load_phdr(). The inner logic is

  labels) differs.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  managing per-segment failure and unwind cleanly is much easier
  with one segment's handling in a dedicated function.

## cc832444 -- [kernel_yield] Introduce
   save_current_kernel_task_state() in process32.c

Commit: cc832444b8...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 27 18:58:37 2018 +0300

> The current change updates the macro used by kernel_yield() and
> panic_save_current_state() to save all the registers and make it
> call a dedicated (new) function called
> save_current_kernel_task_state() instead of the common one,
> save_current_task_state() used by the timer handler before
> calling the scheduler. This allows the new save state C function
> to just use memcpy() to save the state, avoiding any tricky
> calculations caused by the difference in the data saved on stack
> by the CPU when there been a privilege level change and when
> there hasn't.

AI notes:

What changed:

  +55 / -39 across entry.S (+51 / -19) and process32.c (+43 / -24).
  New C function save_current_kernel_task_state() specifically for
  kernel-mode yield / panic paths. entry.S asm macro feeding
  kernel_yield is updated to push a fully populated iret frame so
  the C side can memcpy it wholesale.

Context (from body):

  Without CPL transition, the CPU pushes only EIP+CS+EFLAGS (no
  SS/ESP) onto the stack at interrupt time. Mixing
  user-interrupted and kernel-interrupted paths into a single
  save routine required branchy pointer arithmetic based on the
  saved CS. Splitting the kernel-task path into its own helper
  lets it assume a fixed layout and just memcpy the saved regs.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## d3bffd06 -- [tasklet] Use always kernel_yield() instead of
   kcond_wait in DEBUG builds

Commit: d3bffd0636...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 28 12:37:51 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +9 / -4 in kernel/tasklet.c. Under #ifdef DEBUG, the tasklet
  runner loop skips kcond_wait and instead calls kernel_yield()
  unconditionally when idle.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  In DEBUG builds we want the scheduler + kernel_yield path to
  get maximum exercise; skipping the efficient kcond_wait forces
  the runner to cycle through yield every iteration, stressing
  preemption and context-switch correctness. Release builds keep
  the efficient wait.

## f55024d4 -- [entry] Make kernel context switch funcs use the
   pushed-on-stack EIP

Commit: f55024d4e9...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 28 17:08:27 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +17 / -13 across entry.S and process32.c. The kernel-mode
  context-switch asm now reads the resume EIP from the saved
  struct regs (which already holds the return EIP pushed by the
  CPU at int/yield time) instead of getting it by a separate

  convention.

## d6a6a930 -- [entry] Add 'cld' in asm_int_handler before calling the
   C code

Commit: d6a6a93000...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 28 20:45:08 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +3 / -2 lines in entry.S. `cld` (clear direction flag) inserted
  in asm_int_handler before the call into C.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  x86 ABI / SysV convention assumes DF=0 at function entry so
  `rep movs` / `rep stos` default to forward. An interrupted user
  could have left DF=1; without `cld` the inline-asm memcpy/memset
  introduced a few commits ago would run backwards and corrupt
  memory. Same reason the Linux kernel has the exact same `cld`
  in its interrupt prologue.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## fa6d7194 -- [process32, entry] Re-design the context switch for
   kernel threads

Commit: fa6d719429...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 29 12:45:28 2018 +0300

> Currently, kernel threads and the kernel part of the user
> threads (tasks) had a dedicated copy of the 'regs' struct in
> task_info. The save of kernel context and the switch logic was
> similar to one used for user tasks, except for some trickery
> necessary to handle the fact that in case of no privilege
> change, x86 CPUs don't push esp and ss on the stack. The
> dedicated copy of 'regs' for the kernel state was first pushed
> on stack by asm_int_handler or by kernel_yield and then stored
> in current->kernel_state_regs by either save_current_task_state()
> [preemption] or save_current_kernel_task_state() [yield]. The
> stack used by the int handler/yield to save the registers was
> discarded. Now instead, current->kernel_state_regs has become a
> pointer to a 'regs' struct pointing exactly to that part of the
> stack. This way, the context switch among kernel threads is
> faster and we save some memory too.

AI notes:

What changed:

  +40 / -111 across 6 files -- large net simplification (-71
  lines). entry.S shrinks dramatically (+17 / -40). process32.c
  loses 35 net lines (saving helpers gone). process.h:
  kernel_state_regs becomes a pointer rather than an embedded
  struct. hal.h, debug_utils.c, misc.c adjust dereferences.

Context (from body):

  Elegant fix: instead of copying the saved regs off the stack
  into a per-task storage area (and then switching back), just
  remember where on the stack the saved frame lives. The stack
  itself owns the memory; no copy, no duplicated "which variant
  of the layout do we have" logic. This sheds both CPU time (no
  memcpy on yield) and memory (no embedded regs in task_info).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 4a870b0c -- [process32, entry] Polishing the code

Commit: 4a870b0c3e...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 29 14:26:03 2018 +0300

AI notes:

  +21 / -27 across entry.S and process32.c. Net -6 lines.

  switch path from fa6d7194.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Standard "polish pass" after a substantial refactor -- trim
  leftover scaffolding, align style, remove now-redundant
  comments/decls.

## 6bec50c5 -- [process32, entry] Remove
   save_current_kernel_task_state()

Commit: 6bec50c576...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 29 14:48:49 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +10 / -16 across entry.S (1 line) and process32.c (+9 / -15).
  The dedicated save_current_kernel_task_state() helper
  introduced in cc832444 is deleted; its single remaining caller
  inlines the minimal work still needed.

  a thin shim and can be removed.

## d91c6cd6 -- [process32, entry] Make again the panic being able to
   show the right regs

Commit: d91c6cd61a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 29 20:11:03 2018 +0300

> After the recent changes in the kernel tasks context switch
> code, the panic_save_current_state() got broken, because saving
> just the esp does not work, if the panic save function has to
> return and store the esp. Therefore, user's state_regs has been
> used as a store in this unfortunate corner case.

AI notes:

What changed:

  +60 / -20 across entry.S and process32.c. Panic-path saving is
  restored to full-regs semantics: the old user-space state_regs
  struct is repurposed as the storage for the panic snapshot, so
  panic_save_current_state() can return to its caller without
  losing the registers to print.

Context (from body):

  Regression caused by the recent "stack-pointer only" save
  design. It assumed the caller never returns -- true for yield
  and preemption, but panic_save_current_state() does need to
  return so the panic handler can continue. Reusing state_regs
  is an acceptable hack because during panic the user state is
  moot anyway.

## 0001e5bd -- [interrupts] Make enable/disable interrupts to take
   a uptr* parameter

Commit: 0001e5bd96...

Date:   Fri Mar 30 12:13:41 2018 +0300

What changed:

## 7284d1ea -- [context_switch] Use a single function for both user

## 77ae4b62 -- Move private header paging_int.h to the arch/i386
   source directory

Commit: 77ae4b628c...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Apr 3 10:40:46 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  Pure rename: include/exos/arch/i386/paging_int.h ->
  kernel/arch/i386/paging_int.h. paging.c updates its -I / include
  path accordingly (+3 / -1 lines in paging.c).

Context (guess -- from subject):

  "Private" header (internal-to-the-translation-unit types) has
  no business in the public include/ tree. Moving it next to its
  sole consumer makes the scope explicit and shrinks the include
  search surface.

## 5f24066d -- [paging] Make all the user mapped pages to be
   ref-counted

Commit: 5f24066d35...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Apr 3 11:23:52 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +20 / -22 in kernel/arch/i386/paging.c. map_page() path for
  user pages now unconditionally bumps the frame refcount;
  unmap_page() decrements. Previously only COW/shared pages
  were refcounted; private user pages were not.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Prereq for correct teardown across fork/exec and for future
  mmap semantics. With uniform refcounting, free-on-last-ref
  works whether the page is originally private or shared --
  pdir_destroy can just drop all refs without per-case logic.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## d42bf010 -- [paging] Use just 1 bit flag for COW pages

Commit: d42bf010c1...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Apr 3 15:06:41 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +9 / -7 in kernel/arch/i386/paging.c. The COW marker is
  consolidated into a single bit in a per-frame metadata word
  (instead of a multi-bit field or separate storage).

Context (guess -- from subject):

  After 5f24066d introduced uniform refcounting, the COW flag
  no longer needs to coexist with other per-page attributes in a
  full byte/word -- one bit is enough, freeing bits for other
  metadata.

## 63539df8 -- [threads][step 1] Rename task_info->pid to tid

Commit: 63539df8ad...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Apr 3 18:58:01 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +27 / -27 across 7 files. Pure rename of the task_info.pid
  field to task_info.tid everywhere it's read/written.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  First step toward real POSIX threads. A task_info is per
  thread, not per process; the field was mis-named. Future
  steps (which are clearly coming in this series) will
  introduce a separate process-level pid that multiple tasks
  can share.

## 9b157e2c -- [threads][step 3] Introduce create_new_pid()

  (likely in sched.c) centralises pid allocation; process32.c,

## 28081619 -- [threads][step 5] Make create_new_pid() to return at
   most MAX_PID

Commit: 28081619de...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Apr 3 19:52:46 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +20 / -6 across 4 files. sched.c +16 net: create_new_pid()
  now tracks allocated pids (likely a bitmap or cycling
  counter) and wraps at MAX_PID instead of growing unbounded.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  POSIX requires pids to fit in a pid_t (typically <= 32768).
  Capping at MAX_PID and reusing freed slots mirrors Linux's
  behaviour.

## d5206a92 -- [threads][step 8] Sched: add tree_by_tid in task_info

Commit: d5206a9272...

Date:   Wed Apr 4 19:47:40 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +56 / -9 across 5 files. sched.c +36 net: introduces an AVL
  tree indexed by tid for O(log n) task lookup. task_info gains
  a tree_by_tid node field. avl_bintree.c +8 (helper used by
  sched), process32.c +7 / -0 (insert on task creation),
  process.c +3 (insert after fork).

  lookups for signal delivery, waitpid, /proc, etc.

## 631142b9 -- [threads][step 13] Introduce process_info

Commit: 631142b94b...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 5 15:57:11 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +70 / -47 across 4 files. process.h +23 net: new
  process_info struct carrying per-process state (pid, pdir,
  cwd, ...) that was previously stored per-task_info.
  process.c +42 / -14 creates / initialises process_info on
  fork. fs_syscalls.c switches to reading current->pi->cwd
  etc. process32.c adjusts.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  process (not a thread) move into a new struct shared by all
  threads of the same process. Enables future clone()/
  pthread_create() where multiple task_infos point at one
  process_info.

## 04067bfe -- [avl_bintree] Implement bintree_in_order_visit_internal
   without recursion

Commit: 04067bfe7a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 5 22:38:01 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +63 / -23 across 2 files. avl_bintree.c +49 net: in-order
  traversal rewritten to use an explicit stack instead of
  recursion (Morris or classic stack-based). kmalloc.c +8 /
  -4: likely switches from its own recursive walk to using
  the new iterative one.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Kernel stacks are small (4-16KB typical); recursive tree
  walks can blow the stack on deep imbalances. Iterative
  version bounds stack use to O(log n) heap nodes.

## 593073db -- [kmalloc] Use common/norec.h to avoid recursion

Commit: 593073db2a...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Apr 6 14:25:28 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +48 / -89 across 2 files. kernel/kmalloc.c -47 net: its
  recursive buddy-tree walk deleted in favour of norec.h.
  norec.h gets +4 net (small API polish).

Context (guess -- from subject):

  The buddy allocator's split/merge operations were recursive
  walks of its buddy tree. With ~16KB kernel stacks, a deeply
  fragmented allocator could blow up. Switching to the
  explicit-stack walker makes kmalloc stack-safe.

## d2aed0ca -- [threads][step 19] Implement create_new_pid() in a
   more efficient way

Commit: d2aed0caf3...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Apr 6 18:05:08 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +55 / -9 across 2 files. sched.c +52 net: create_new_pid()
  now uses a bitmap / AVL ordered by tid to find the first
  free pid quickly instead of linear-scanning the task tree.
  avl_bintree.c +3 (helper).

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Linear search for next free pid becomes O(n) as tasks
  accumulate. Bitmap lookup (or tree gap-finding) is O(log n)
  or amortised O(1).

  `access = DPL0 | TYPE_CODE | PRESENT`, replacing magic
  0x9A / 0x92 / 0xFA / 0xF2 constants.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Payoff of 7c6eb9fc: readable, auditable GDT entry
  setup. When something breaks, the flag is obvious.

## 577852e3 -- [interrupts] Use a separate code path for IRQs

Commit: 577852e35d...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Apr 8 12:12:55 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +52 / -19 across entry.S, irq_handlers.S, isr_handlers.S,
  interrupts.c. IRQ dispatch no longer funnels through the
  shared ISR common stub; irq_handlers.S has its own common
  tail that calls a specialised handle_irq() in the C code.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Exception and IRQ flows have different responsibilities
  (error codes vs PIC EOI) but were sharing a common prologue.
  Splitting lets each path omit code the other needs, at the
  cost of a touch of duplication.

## 0a18c365 -- [interrupts] Don't validate stack ptr in case of
   faults

Commit: 0a18c36563...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Apr 11 13:39:30 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  1 line in kernel/interrupts.c. The push_nested_interrupt
  stack-pointer sanity check is skipped for exception
  vectors (faults).

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Faults can fire with an unusual/corrupt stack (stack
  overflow, bad pointer deref); asserting on ESP bounds
  turns a recoverable fault into a double-panic. Fault
  handlers must tolerate weirdness.

## b0e87fce -- [ldt] Using load_ldt() in switch_to_task() does not
   cause GPF anymore

Commit: b0e87fce53...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Apr 11 13:51:46 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +6 / -13 across 4 files. Small adjustments in gdt.c,
  gdt_int.h, idt.c, process32.c. Exact fix probably
  involves re-ordering lldt vs segment-register reloads.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Previous commit's LDT-load caused #GP. Subject phrasing
  ("does not cause GPF anymore") confirms this commit is
  the fix. Typical cause: loading an LDT selector before
  the LDT itself is installed, or DS/ES pointing into a
  now-invalid descriptor.

## 3919dc8e -- [set_thread_area] Add critical checks preventing user

## 8c62f077 -- [gtests] Using C++'s features to remove the macros

Commit: 8c62f0772f...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 12 20:50:36 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +157 / -130 in unittests/itoa.cpp. Net +27 but scope
  is very different -- preprocessor macros (used to
  generate per-type tests) replaced by C++ templates,
  type_traits, snprintf-based golden comparisons.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Macros in C++ tests are a smell: they lose type info,
  confuse IDEs, and break debuggers. Templates
  accomplish the same fan-out with type safety.
