## 6ffa275c -- [printk] Copying (+fork) its code from common/ to
   bootloader and kernel

Commit: 6ffa275c80...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Apr 13 12:57:43 2018 +0300

> This change is necessary in order to extend the kernel
> implementation of printk() without affecting the
> minimal one used for the bootloader. Its the same
> happened for 'term'.

AI notes:

What changed:

  +183 / -95 across 5 files. common/string_util.c -94:
  printk code leaves. New bootloader/basic_printk.c (97
  lines) and kernel/printk.c (85 lines) each own a
  copy. basic_term.h moves into the bootloader dir.
  stage3.c 1-line include adjust.

Context (from body):

  The common-code "printk with weak linkage" trick
  (commit 133dcb0b, step 6 of the header reorg) worked
  but kept kernel and bootloader tied to one source.
  Forking lets the kernel printk grow features (log
  levels, ring buffer, lock) without bloating the
  bootloader.

## db641bbf -- [sys_writev] Make it run with preemption disabled

Commit: db641bbfff...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Apr 13 13:08:24 2018 +0300

> At the moment there are still no filesystem locks in
> exOS, therefore just preemption is disabled. Still,
> sys_writev() needed the preemption to be disabled since
> it has to behave like a single write(). No other writes
> can interfere.

AI notes:

What changed:

  +7 / -2 in fs_syscalls.c. sys_writev brackets its iovec
  loop with disable_preemption / enable_preemption.

Context (from body):

  Atomicity: writev is supposed to be equivalent to a
  single write of the concatenated buffers. Without FS
  locks the only way to prevent interleaved writes from
  other tasks is to keep preemption off for the duration.

## a56eb056 -- [printk] Make it use a ringbuffer in case of nested
   [e.g. IRQ] calls

Commit: a56eb0566f...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Apr 13 19:15:18 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +152 / -15 across 6 files. printk.c +113 net: adds a
  ring buffer; when printk is called while another printk
  is already executing (nested via IRQ), the new call
  appends to the ringbuf and returns. The outer call's
  flush step drains the ringbuf. interrupts.c +22:
  hook to trigger drain on IRQ return. kb.c, timer_handler
  emit marker prints to exercise the path. basic_defs.h
  +5.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  The term_write path is not re-entrant (holds no lock
  and manipulates cursor state). Without this, a printk
  from an IRQ handler interleaving with a concurrent
  printk would scramble the screen. Ringbuf defers the
  nested print until it's safe to flush.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## b68aca4e -- [printk] Fix a bug in printk_flush() by adding
   minibuf

Commit: b68aca4ece...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Apr 14 11:48:41 2018 +0300

> The problem: with the previous impl. we first claim in
> the do-while loop that we have read the data from the
> ringbuf and then we actually read it (while writing to
> term). The problem with that approach is that if another
> printk occurs (3rd nested call), it will find the used
> field = 0 and so will use up to sizeof(printk_rbuf) for
> appending its data, corrupting this way that the 2nd
> nested call was about to read. The solution is to use
> a minibuf in the do-while loop and, each time, copy the
> data safely on the stack. In the worst case when the
> loop has to iterate more then once, we'll just have to
> re-read the data.
>
> BONUS: this commit also adds term_write_char2(c, color)
> to term.h allowing its callers to write a char using a
> specific color without changing the current color.

AI notes:

What changed:

  +48 / -30 across 4 files. printk.c +27 net implements
  the minibuf fix: copy to a small stack buffer first,
  then write to term. term.c +10 net: new
  term_write_char2(c, color). term.h +1 decl.
  timer_handler.c 1-line adjust.

Context (from body):

  Classic TOCTOU on a single-producer/single-consumer
  ring. Fix is to read-then-commit, not commit-then-read.
  Commit message is a textbook example of capturing a
  subtle concurrency bug.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 170f5134 -- Introduce copy_from_user() and make it to work in
   sys_write()

Commit: 170f51341d...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Apr 14 14:50:27 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +97 / -12 across 7 files. New header exos/user.h (14
  lines) declaring copy_from_user / copy_to_user. New
  kernel/arch/i386/user.c (39 lines) with the i386
  impl that catches faults (probably via a fixup table
  checked in page_fault_handler). paging.c +12 / -4:
  page-fault handler recognises the fixup and returns
  an error. fs_syscalls.c switches sys_write to use
  copy_from_user. printk.c +4 / -2 likely uses it for
  %s. debug_utils.c +3 / -1.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Foundational security primitive: kernel must never
  dereference user pointers without a mechanism to
  handle bad addresses. copy_from_user is the standard
  Unix idiom. This commit is the seed -- more syscalls
  converted in the following commits.

## 2ec124ce -- [sys_writev] Use copy_from_user() for iov

## c271d968 -- [process] Introduce per-task copybufs and make write
   and writev to use them

Commit: c271d96828...
Author: Vladislav Valtchev <vladislav.valtchev@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Apr 14 19:46:18 2018 +0300

AI notes:

What changed:

  +32 / -11 across 3 files. process.h +4: task_info gains
  a per-task kmalloc'd copy buffer. process.c +17 net
  allocates/frees it with the task. fs_syscalls.c
  switches sys_write / sys_writev to this buffer instead
  of stack / per-call kmalloc.

Context (guess -- from subject):

  Performance: avoid kmalloc on every syscall, avoid
  deep stack usage for user-copies. Per-task buffer is
  a good compromise (no locking required, reused across
  syscalls).
